Ken Leahy Constr., Inc. v. Cascade Gen., Inc.


SC S44812


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


329 Ore. 566; 994 P.2d 112; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 1032


November 2, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
December 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration dismissed by Ken Leahy Constr. v. Cascade Gen., 2000 Ore. LEXIS 394 (Or., May 25, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 9307-04717; CA A85442. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


*  Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, 149 Ore. App. 480, 944 P.2d 951 (1997).


Ken Leahy Constr. v. Cascade Gen., 149 Ore. App. 480, 944 P.2d 951, 1997 Ore. App. LEXIS 1119 (1997)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversing the award of declaratory judgment to plaintiff in plaintiff's action for breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff construction company and defendant developer entered into an agreement for plaintiff to construct a ship repair facility for defendant. When defendant failed to find a tenant for the property, it refused to assume responsibility for the facility. Plaintiff sought declaratory judgment that defendant breached the contract and requested injunctive relief. The court granted plaintiff's request. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that there was no evidence that defendant owned the dry docks and specific performance was improper. On further appeal, the court reversed and reinstated the judgment of the trial court, holding that under state statutes the trial court had the authority to declare defendant to be an owner of the facility even though the purchase price had not been paid. The record supported the conclusion that a contract existed, and that the parties had agreed that defendant was the owner of the dry docks.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and reinstated the judgment of the trial court, holding that defendant was the owner of the ship repair facility under a contract entered into between plaintiff and defendant.

 

2 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sutherland


SC S46458


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


329 Ore. 359; 987 P.2d 501; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 603


September 8, 1999, Argued and Submitted  
October 7, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 983427CR.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ to issue. Pursuant to ORAP 1.20(4), 11.17, and 14.05(2)(c), and notwithstanding ORAP 9.25, a combined peremptory writ and appellate judgment shall issue on October 11, 1999, unless a petition for reconsideration is both filed and physically received by the Office of the State Court Administrator by October 8, 1999. Any timely petition for reconsideration will stay issuance of the peremptory writ and appellate judgment until the court acts on such petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a peremptory writ of mandamus to overturn the order of the Klamath County Circuit Court (Oregon), granting pretrial release to defendant on the basis that a state mandatory bail statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with second-degree assault. Petitioner, the State of Oregon, filed an original mandamus proceeding in the state's highest court to overturn the order of the circuit court, which granted defendant pretrial release. Petitioner argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.240(5) mandated that the court impose a $ 50,000 bond before release. After granting an alternative writ, the court first held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.240(4) was facially unconstitutional in light of Or. Const. art. I, § 14, which required courts to set bail for defendants accused of crimes other than murder or treason. The court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.240(5) was not facially unconstitutional, because Or. Const. art. I, § 16, which bars excessive bail, impliedly guaranteed defendant a hearing to contest imposition of the $ 50,000 bail on an as-applied basis. The court issued the peremptory writ in favor of petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ in favor of petitioner, reasoning that the portion of a state statute setting minimum bail for certain crimes was valid, because the Oregon constitution impliedly granted defendant a hearing to contest the minimum bail amount.

 

3 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Lakin v. Senco Prods., Inc.


SC S44110


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


329 Ore. 369; 987 P.2d 476; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 699; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,696



October 7, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 9211-07901; CA A83575.



DISPOSITION: Opinion clarified; legal interest on the jury's full award of noneconomic damages accrues from the date when the trial court entered judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner moved for clarification as to the date interest began to accrue on the additional portion of a modified award of noneconomic damages to respondents in their suit against petitioner for negligent failure to warn and product liability.


OVERVIEW: Respondents sued petitioner seeking economic, noneconomic, and punitive damages related to their claims of negligent failure to warn and product liability. However, state law that capped noneconomic damage awards served to reduce the awards jury found for respondents. On appeal, court had held the state law capping the awards was unconstitutional. In determining when interest should accrue on the additional portion of the non-capped awards, petitioner argued no interest should be added to the additional portions of the awards, as a final modified judgment had yet to be entered by trial court. Respondents contended interest began to accrue on the additional amount as of the date trial court entered judgment on the verdict. Following controlling case law, court held interest on the award as modified ran from the date of the original judgment.


OUTCOME: Court found interest on full award of economic damages began to accrue from the date trial court entered the initial judgment.

 

4 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


FEVES v. KITZHABER (In re THE CONSTITUTIONALITY OF SENATE BILL 686 OREGONIANS FOR HEALTH)


SC S46770


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


329 Ore. 339; 986 P.2d 1167; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 597


September 10, 1999, Argued and Submitted  
September 16, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] S46771.



DISPOSITION: The petition for review is dismissed. The petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed both a petition for review and a petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus, seeking a decision invalidating the emergency clause in legislation concerning the siting of a women's correctional facility and intake center complex so that plaintiffs could attempt to have the legislation referred to the voters under Or. Const. art. IV, § 1(3)(a).


OVERVIEW: An emergency clause passed during a legislative session. Plaintiffs filed a petition for review and a petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus, seeking a decision invalidating the emergency clause. The underlying question was whether SB 686 was an act regulating taxation or exemption under Or. Const. art. IX, § 1a, for which the legislative assembly could not declare an emergency. The court dismissed the petition for review and denied the petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus. The court held that the court lacked jurisdiction to review the constitutionality of the act because the legislature did not include the particular section within the ambit of the court's statutorily authorized original jurisdiction, and the court could not insert into a statute that which has been omitted. Moreover, the court held that nothing in the context of SB 686 suggested a construction other than that mandated by the express wording of the act. The court held further that that act did nothing more than contemplate the potential for condemnation. Neither it effected directly nor by implication, any change in the existing law regulating taxation or exemption.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition for review and denied the petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus, holding that the court lacked jurisdiction to review the constitutionality of the act because the legislature did not include the particular section within the ambit of the court's statutorily authorized original jurisdiction. The court held further that the act did not effect any change in the existing law regulating taxation or exemption.

 

5 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simonsen


SC S43487


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


329 Ore. 288; 986 P.2d 566; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 559


May 8, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
August 12, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 340.
Writ of certiorari denied Simonsen v. Oregon, 528 U.S. 1090, 120 S. Ct. 822, 145 L. Ed. 2d 692, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 340 (2000)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Simonsen v. Premo, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1774 (Or. Ct. App., Dec. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 88CR-1816. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Coos County Circuit Court. Richard L. Barron, Judge.
State v. Simonsen, 319 Ore. 510, 878 P.2d 409, 1994 Ore. LEXIS 78 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On automatic and direct review of the judgment of defendant's conviction for aggravated murder and a sentence of death imposed by the Coos County Circuit Court (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction of aggravated murder and the sentence of death entered in his third sentencing-phase proceeding were on automatic and direct review. The supreme court considered defendant's several assignments of error. Not all assignments warranted discussion. Under Or. Rev. Stat. § 135.365, defendant was not entitled to withdraw his guilty pleas because the trial court had entered judgment concerning his guilt at the time of his motion. There was no abuse of discretion by the trial court in ruling that an inadvertent and passing reference to defendant's earlier death sentence during voir dire did not require the dismissal of the jury panel. The trial court did not err by refusing defendant's requested jury instruction regarding consecutive sentences because it was legally inaccurate. Defendant assigned error to several statements that plaintiff made during its closing argument. Defendant failed to demonstrate how some of those statements, which referred to evidence already before the jury, resulted in prejudice. There was no abuse of discretion in denying defendant's motion for mistrial; nor did the trial court err in not declaring a mistrial sua sponte.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of conviction for aggravated murder and sentence of death. None of defendant's assignments of error provided a basis for reversal. There was no error or abuse of discretion by the trial court.

 

6 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Lakin v. Senco Prods., Inc.


SC S44110


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


329 Ore. 62; 987 P.2d 463; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 419; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,571


November 5, 1997, Argued and Submitted; June 11, 1998, Resubmitted  
July 15, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 9211-07901; CA A83575. On review from the Court of Appeals. *.


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Ancer L. Haggerty, Judge. 144 Ore. App. 52, 925 P.2d 107 (1996).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed an order of the Oregon Court of Appeals, affirming the lower court's entry of judgment for plaintiffs upon plaintiffs' personal injury action and holding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 18.560(1) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Following serious injury caused by a nail gun, plaintiffs sued defendant corporation upon negligence and strict products liability theories, seeking damages. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiff and awarded economic damages. Under Or. Rev. Stat. § 18.560(1), the trial court limited noneconomic damage to $ 500,000 for each plaintiff. Both sides appealed, and the intermediate court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 18.560(1) violated the constitution. On appeal, the court affirmed and remanded for entry of the original noneconomic damage award. § 18.560(1) violated Or. Const. art. 1, § 17 by abridging the right to jury trial. The damage cap mandated by § 18.560(1) denied plaintiffs a second jury trial and reduced the jury award even where the award was not considered excessive in light of the evidence. The denial of defendant's motion for directed verdict upon the issue of punitive damages was not clear error, and the amount awarded to plaintiffs was rational in light of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for plaintiffs and the finding that the statute was unconstitutional; the limitation on noneconomic damages impermissibly violated the jury's resolution of a factual inquiry; the court also upheld the award of punitive damages.

 

7 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Dale v. Myers


SC S46044


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


328 Ore. 466; 980 P.2d 157; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 256


March 16, 1999, Argued and Submitted  
May 14, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Ballot title certified as modified. This decision shall become effective in accordance with ORAP 11.30(10).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, who were electors that timely submitted written comments, challenged the Oregon Attorney General's certified ballot title for a proposed initiative measure and sought modification by the court under Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.085(2).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were electors who submitted timely written comments to a certified ballot title by the Oregon Attorney General for a proposed initiative measure, thereby challenging the ballot title under Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.085(2). Specifically, petitioners challenged the caption and the "yes" and "no" vote result statements, arguing that such items were not in compliance with the requirements for ballot titles set out in Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.035. The court concluded that the caption failed to comply substantially with the statutory requirement that it reasonably identify the subject matter of the measure, under § 250.035(2)(a), because it swept too broadly and was thus insufficient to inform the reader of the measure's principal subject. The court therefore modified the caption. As to the result statements, the court found that they were in substantial compliance with Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.035(2)(b)(c), despite their being worded similarly to the ballot title caption. Moreover, the court found that the "no" statement made it clear just what the result of voting "no" would be, despite petitioners' assertions to the contrary. Only the caption, then, was ordered as modified.


OUTCOME: The court modified the caption of the certified ballot title because it failed to substantially comply with statutory requirement that it reasonably identify the subject matter of the measure because it swept too broadly and was thus insufficient to inform the reader of the measure's principal subject. The court also found that "yes" and "no" vote result statements did comply with the statute, despite their similar wording with the caption.

 

8 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baker


SC S45664


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


328 Ore. 355; 976 P.2d 1132; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 127


November 10, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
April 1, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC CR980-1016.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State government petitioned for a writ of mandamus from an order of the Clackamas County Circuit Court (Oregon), which held that the respondent criminal defendant could choose to waive his right to a trial.


OVERVIEW: Respondent criminal defendant was charged with multiple felony offenses. Before trial, the respondent executed a waiver of jury trial. The petitioner state then demanded a trial, notwithstanding respondent's waiver, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.001(1). The respondent objected, arguing that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court agreed with respondent and ruled that the case would be tried without a hearing. The petitioner then brought a mandamus proceeding. The court stated that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.001, the respondent had the right to waive her right to a jury trial. The court held that Or. Const. Art. I, § 11 granted the trial judge discretionary choice to deny a criminal defendant in a non-capital criminal case the right to waive trial by jury. The court further held that the legislature's choice to provide the right to the district attorney to insist on a jury trial in Or. Rev. Stat. 136.001(1) infringed respondent's rights. Therefore, the trial court did not err in refusing to recognize the state's demand for a jury trial. The petition for writ of mandamus was denied.


OUTCOME: The petitioner's writ of mandamus was denied because the respondent had a constitutional right to waive her right to a jury trial in her criminal prosecution.

 

9 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rangel


SC S44151


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


328 Ore. 294; 977 P.2d 379; 1999 Ore. LEXIS 71


September 10, 1997, Argued and Submitted; September 30, 1998, Resubmitted  
February 26, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 95-0127CM; CA A91166. On review from the Court of Appeals *.


*  Appeal from Hood River County Circuit Court, Paul Crowley, Judge. 146 Ore. App. 571, 934 P.2d 1128 (1997).


State v. Rangel, 146 Ore. App. 571, 934 P.2d 1128, 1997 Ore. App. LEXIS 211 (1997)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversing the judgment of the trial court, which held that Oregon's stalking statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.732, was overbroad in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and U.S. Const. amend. I and was not capable of judicial narrowing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with stalking in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.732. The trial court determined that § 163.732 was overbroad in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and U.S. Const. amend. I and that the statute was not capable of judicial narrowing. The lower court reversed the trial court's decision. On further appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's decision. Although there were instances of potential impermissible application of § 163.732, the court was able to interpret the statute to eliminate any overbreadth. As construed, § 163.732 was not facially overbroad under Or. Const. art. I, § 8, because under § 163.732, a contact based on communication was limited to threats that were so unambiguous, unequivocal, and specific to the addressee that they convincingly expressed to the address the intention that they would be carried out. This construction eliminated overbreadth while maintaining reasonable fidelity to the legislature's words and apparent intent. Similarly, when the court construed § 163.732 to require genuine threat and intent to carry out the threat, the statute was not facially overbroad under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision because Oregon's stalking statute was not facially overbroad under the free speech protections of the federal and state Constitution where the statute was construed to require genuine threat and intent to carry out the threat.

 

10 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Fidanque v. State by and Through Oregon Gov't Stds. & Practices Comm'n


SC S43705


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


328 Ore. 1; 969 P.2d 376; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 1017


May 9, 1997, Argued and Submitted; June 11, 1998, Resubmitted  
November 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 94C-11492; CA A86332. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


*  Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Paul Lipscomb, Judge. 141 Ore. App. 495, 920 P.2d 154 (1996).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner lobbyists challenged, in the trial court, the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 171.743, which required lobbyists to pay a registration fee. The trial court found the statute unconstitutional, but the Oregon Court of Appeals reversed. The lobbyists sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Or. Rev. Stat. § 171.743 applied to the lobbyists who were defined by their participation in the primarily expressive activity of lobbying. Their lobbying was political speech, and being a lobbyist was the act of being a communicator to the legislature on political subjects. Section 171.743 imposed a fee for engaging in that activity. The fee was imposed for the purpose of funding a government agency that was responsible for tasks other than registering the lobbyists. The argument that the fee was actually a reasonable approximation of the cost of operating the lobbyist registration program was not supported by the fact that the statute on its face did not tie its fee to the costs associated with registering lobbyists. Additionally, the history relied on to support that argument was not sufficiently detailed to allow the appellate court to determine whether the criteria used in estimating the cost of registering a lobbyist were meaningful for constitutional purposes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

11 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Leo v. Keisling


SC S45677


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


327 Ore. 556; 964 P.2d 1023; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 900


September 15, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
October 7, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 98C-17232; CA A103357. On certification from the Court of Appeals. *.


*  Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Richard D. Barber, Judge. Order from the Court of Appeals dated September 2, 1998.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court is reversed. The case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings. Pursuant to ORAP 1.20(4), and notwithstanding ORAP 14.05(3)(b), the State Court Administrator shall issue the appellate judgment at 12:00 p.m. on Monday, October 12, 1998, unless a petition for reconsideration is both filed with and received by the office of the State Court Administrator by that time. Any timely petition for reconsideration will stay issuance of the appellate judgment until the court acts on such petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed to the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which certified the appeal to the court, after the circuit court rejected plaintiffs' claims for declaratory and injunctive relief and entered judgment for defendants, Secretary of State and State of Oregon, in an action alleging the secretary exceeded his authority in declaring that a certain initiative qualified for a general election ballot.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action in circuit court, alleging that the secretary exceeded his authority by declaring that a certain initiative petition qualified for a general election ballot. They sought a declaration that the petition had insufficient signatures for placement on the ballot. They also sought to enjoin the secretary from certifying the petition to the ballot or, alternatively, from taking any further action to place that petition on the ballot. The circuit court rejected plaintiffs' claims for declaratory and injunctive relief and entered judgment for defendants. Plaintiffs appealed and the appellate court certified the appeal to the court, which reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case. The court resolved the case on a subconstitutional basis. The court concluded that the provision of Or. Admin. R. 165-014-0030 that allowed the secretary to qualify an initiative petition for the ballot even though the secretary was up to 80 percent certain that the petition did not contain the required number of signatures violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.105(4), the statute pursuant to which Rule 165-014-0030 was promulgated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court that rejected plaintiffs' claims for declaratory and injunctive relief in an action alleging the secretary had exceeded his authority in declaring that a certain initiative qualified for a general election ballot. The court remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

12 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hayward


SC S43096


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


327 Ore. 397; 963 P.2d 667; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 593


May 4, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
July 24, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Haugen, 349 Ore. 174, 243 P.3d 31, 2010 Ore. LEXIS 829 (2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hayward v. Belleque, 248 Ore. App. 141, 273 P.3d 926, 2012 Ore. App. LEXIS 152 (2012)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Hayward v. Premo, 281 Ore. App. 113, 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1084 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 10-94-08860. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and the sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court of Lane County. Pierre L. Van Rysselberghe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and the sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and death sentence, entered in the Circuit Court of Lane County (Oregon), for aggravated murder, intentional murder, felony murder, attempted aggravated murder, first-degree assault, first-degree kidnapping, first-degree robbery, and first-degree burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with others, committed a robbery at a convenience store and murdered the employees of the store. The defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. The defendant appealed his conviction and sentence on grounds that evidence about death metal music and satanism was not relevant, and therefore, was inadmissible. In addition, the defendant appealed on grounds that he was improperly denied a plea offer. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court held that prosecutorial discretion regarding plea bargaining did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 20 where that discretion was exercised in the context of a coherent, systematic policy. In addition, the court held that, pursuant to Or. Evid. Code 403, relevant evidence could be excluded only if its probative value was substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice. Finally, the court held that in a prosecution for any criminal homicide, a photograph of the victim while alive would be admissible evidence when offered by the district attorney to show the general appearance and condition of the victim while alive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence of the defendant.

 

13 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Armatta v. Kitzhaber


SC S44995


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


327 Ore. 250; 959 P.2d 49; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 538


March 31, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
June 25, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 96C-14060; CA A96736. On certification from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Pamela L. Abernethy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both plaintiff individuals and defendant state sought review of a judgment from the Marion County Circuit Court (Oregon), which enjoined defendant from enforcing a crime rights initiative and severed one section from the rest of the measure.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff individuals filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief that a crime rights initiative was unconstitutional. The lower court enjoined defendant state from enforcing the initiative and severed one section from the rest of the measure. Both plaintiff and defendant challenged the lower court's judgment. On appeal, the court first concluded that that the measure contained two or more amendments that must be voted upon separately under Or. Const. art. XVII, § 1. Further, the measure was invalid in its entirety because the measure was not passed in compliance with Or. Const. art. XVII, § 1. Also, the court found injunctive relief was not necessary in light of the determination that the measure was not adopted in compliance with the state constitution, and did not address the propriety of the order enjoining defendant from enforcing the measure. Finally, the court reversed the lower court's judgment, which severed the measure from the constitution and enjoined defendant from enforcing the measure. The court affirmed the award of attorney fees to plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which enjoined defendant state from enforcing a crime rights initiative and severed one section from the rest of the measure, because the initiative was not passed in compliance with the state constitution. The court affirmed the award of attorney fees to plaintiff individuals.

 

14 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Vogl v. Department of Revenue


SC S43375 (Control), S43379 (Cases consolidated for argument and opinion)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


327 Ore. 193; 960 P.2d 373; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 530


September 4, 1997, Argued and Submitted  
June 18, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OTC 3605, 3606, 3607, 3608, 3609, 3610. CC 9311-07480; CA A93208. S43375 on appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. S43379 on appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, on certification from the Court of Appeals. Carl N. Byers, Oregon Tax Court, and Nely Johnson, Multnomah County Circuit Court, Judges. Resubmitted June 17, 1998.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Tax Court in Vogl is reversed, and the case is remanded to the Tax Court for further proceedings. The judgment of the circuit court in Dixon is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant retired public employees (taxpayers) sought review of judgments rendered by the Oregon Tax Court and the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon) in favor of respondent Department of Revenue and governmental officials (Department) as to payment of income tax on retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers were retired from federal and state public service. The retired federal taxpayers contended that 1995 Or. Laws 569 was unconstitutional because it created a tax rebate for retired state employees, but not for federal employees. The taxpayers who were federal and state retirees contended that they were due compensation for having paid tax on their state and federal retirement incomes. The court determined that 1995 Or. Laws 569 constituted a tax rebate for state retirees that was not afforded federal retirees even though the statute referred to an increase in compensation. The court determined that the state retirees were not entitled to compensation for tax paid on income attributable to state employment. The court reversed and remanded the cases as to the federal retiree taxpayers, and affirmed the case as to the state retiree taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the Tax Court as to federal retirees, and reversed the decision of the circuit court as to the tax paid on state retirement benefits.

 

15 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Lane Transit Dist. v. Lane County


SC S44061


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


327 Ore. 161; 957 P.2d 1217; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 449


September 9, 1997, Argued and Submitted  
May 29, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 16-95-02904; CA A89559. On review from the Court of Appeals. *.


*  Appeal from Lane County Circuit Court, David V. Brewer, Judge. 146 Ore. App. 109, 932 P.2d 81 (1997).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed in part. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner transit district sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed the judgment of the circuit court, and concluded that the initiative measure was legislative in nature, in favor of defendant county and respondent transit committee.


OVERVIEW: The transit committee filed a proposed initiative measure for a vote by the electors of the transit district, which would have reduced the salary of the transit district's general manager and established procedures by which that salary could have been increased. The transit authority was governed by a board of directors, the members of which were appointed by the governor, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 267.090. The board, in turn, appointed the general manager, who held that office indefinitely, subject to removal by the board, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 267.135. The transit district brought an action against the county, seeking a declaration that the proposed initiative measure was administrative in nature and, therefore, not properly addressed through the initiative process. The circuit court held in favor of the transit district, but the judgment was later reversed by the court of appeals. The court reversed this judgment, by holding that the proposed initiative measure to set the salary and benefits for the general manager was an administrative task and, therefore, not a legislative plan because it did not appoint the general manager nor fix the terms of her employment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the judgment, which reversed the judgment of the circuit court, and concluded that the initiative measure was legislative in nature, in favor of the county and the transit committee. The court also affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the circuit court.

 

16 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Carlile v. Frost


SC S43707*, SC S44065 (consolidated)


* Relating to Linn County Circuit Court Case No. 8802-0368.


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


326 Ore. 607; 956 P.2d 202; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 274


January 6, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
April 1, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CA A94916. An original proceeding in mandamus; on review from an order of dismissal by the Court of Appeals dated January 17, 1997. **.


** Appeal from Linn County Circuit Court, Jackson L. Frost. Judge.



DISPOSITION: On mandamus, the alternative writ of mandamus is denied. On the appeal, the order of dismissal of the Court of Appeals is vacated and the case is remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the state's appeal of the trial court's suppression order during a penalty-phase proceeding. The state also filed a writ of mandamus, challenging the trial court's orders granting in part defendant's evidentiary motion in limine and allowing a jury instruction on the sentencing option of life imprisonment without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for aggravated murder. The sentence was ultimately vacated and the matter remanded to the trial court twice for a penalty-phase proceeding. Before the start of the third penalty-phase proceeding, defendant filed a motion in limine seeking to suppress evidentiary items that the trial court had admitted in earlier guilt-phase and penalty-phase proceedings. The trial court granted the motion in part. The court of appeals dismissed the state's interlocutory appeal. The court vacated the dismissal of the intermediate court holding that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.060(3) the state could take an appeal from an order suppressing evidence before the beginning of a penalty-phase-only retrial. However, the court ruled that the trial court erred in granting the motion in limine because all evidence that was properly admitted in the earlier guilt- and penalty-phase proceedings was also admissible in the new penalty-phase proceeding. Moreover, the court dismissed the state's writ of mandamus that sought to order the trial court to reverse its decision to instruct the jury on the sentencing option of life imprisonment because of laches.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's dismissal of the state's appeal on the evidentiary issue and dismissed its request for a writ of mandamus.

 

17 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Atiyeh v. State


SC S42467


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


326 Ore. 531; 956 P.2d 177; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 270


November 6, 1997, Argued and Submitted  
March 26, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 16-95-00123; CA A90030. On certification from the Court of Appeals pursuant to Oregon Laws 1995, chapter 284. *


*  Appeal from a supplemental judgment of the Lane County Circuit Court, Jack L. Mattison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The supplemental judgment of the circuit court awarding attorney fees is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order entered by the Lane County Circuit Court (Oregon), which awarded attorney fees to plaintiffs, a group of private citizens, present and former public officials, public employee unions, and municipalities.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs initiated a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of an initiative measure. The circuit court entered judgment for plaintiffs on two of their four claims for relief. Both sides appealed the judgment. The circuit court then entered a supplemental judgment awarding plaintiffs attorney fees and the state appealed the supplemental judgment. Subsequently the court dismissed the parties' appeals on the merits as moot and addressed the appeal of the award of attorney fees. The court noted that ordinarily American courts would not award attorney's fees to the prevailing party absent authorization of statute or contract. The court nonetheless retained the inherent, equitable power to award to the prevailing party attorney fees when the prevailing party had succeeded in protecting the rights of others as much as his own. The court held that plaintiffs prevailed in their action, but because the state's appeal was cut short by mootness, the court could not conclude that the judgment actually protected the rights of anyone. The court reversed the supplemental judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the supplemental judgment of the circuit court awarding plaintiffs attorney fees.

 

18 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Pollin v. Department of Revenue


SC S44044


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


326 Ore. 427; 952 P.2d 537; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 18


January 5, 1998, Argued and Submitted  
February 12, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] OTC 3812. On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. * Carl N. Byers, Judge.


*  14 OTR 96 (1997).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Tax Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Oregon Tax Court, which found for respondent Department of Revenue (department) and ruled that Or. Rev. Stat. § 307.110(1) (1995) provided for the taxation of the full value of government property leased to a private enterprise. The taxpayer claimed that only the value of the leasehold was subject to taxation.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer leased government property immediately adjacent to an airport for use as a motor hotel. The department taxed the full value of the property. The tax court upheld the department's decision, ruling that § 307.110(1) provided for taxation of the real market value of the leased land. The court affirmed the judgment below, holding that § 307.110(1) made public property that was leased to a nonexempt taxpayer taxable. Further, § 307.110(1) subjected the property to assessment and taxation at its full value if the lessee had full use of the property for private gain. That the property was held under a lease did not limit taxation to only the value of the leasehold interest. Although under § 307.090(1) government property was generally exempt from taxation, § 307.110 restored to the tax rolls property that § 307.090(1) removed. The court rejected the taxpayer's argument that such an interpretation was unconstitutional as a non-uniform method of taxation. The court also rejected the argument that the lease constituted a governmental restriction on the property's use under § 308.205(2)(d), which limited the value assigned to the property and thus the assessment that was made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that judgment of the tax court which agreed with the department that the full value of the government property leased by the taxpayer was taxable.

 

19 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Foltz v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


SC S43426


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


326 Ore. 294; 952 P.2d 1012; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 7


March 7, 1997, Argued and Submitted  
January 23, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] USDC Civil 94-6293-HO. On certified questions from United States District Court Order dated February 26, 1997. Michael R. Hogan, United States District Judge.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff insured's federal action for the denial or reduction of benefits under the personal injury payment (PIP) provision of her policy, defendant insurer filed a motion to dismiss. The United States District Court for the District of Oregon certified questions regarding mandatory and binding arbitration for PIP disputes under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 742.520(6), 742.522(1).


OVERVIEW: The insurer contended that before the insured could maintain the instant action, she had to first arbitrate the denial or reduction in amount of PIP benefits in accordance with § 742.520(6). The insured contended that § 742.520(6), in combination with § 742.522, violated her right to a jury trial under Or. Const. art. I, § 17. The court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 742.520(6) required the insured to submit to arbitration when the reduction or denial of PIP benefits was based on fraud, negligence, and breach of contract because the actual dispute was still based on a PIP dispute. The court further held that before she proceeded to trial on her claim for damages, the insured first had to arbitrate the reduction or denial of PIP benefits. The court found that Or. Rev. Stat. § 742.522(1) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 17 because it took away a jury trial when it made mandatory arbitration under Or. Rev. Stat. § 742.520(6) binding on the parties. The court held that § 742.520(6) did not violate the insured's right to a jury trial because it only made arbitration mandatory, not binding. Any award made from the mandatory arbitration under § 742.520(6) would not be binding on the insured.


OUTCOME: The court answered yes to the question regarding the requirement of arbitration for PIP disputes prior to court action, and no to the question of whether a plaintiff could establish damages in court without having first arbitrated the dispute. The court further answered yes to the question of whether the state statutory scheme regarding mandatory arbitration violated a plaintiff's right to a jury trial.

Inquiry Concerning a Judge (gallagher)


SC S44156


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


326 Ore. 267; 951 P.2d 705; 1998 Ore. LEXIS 4


November 14, 1997, Argued and Submitted  
January 15, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CJFD 95-96. On review of the recommendation of the Commission on Judicial Fitness and Disability.



DISPOSITION: The accused is suspended from office without salary for a period of six months, commencing on the effective date of this decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court directly reviewed a recommendation of the Commission on Judicial Fitness and Disability (Oregon) in a judicial discipline case, which recommended that a circuit court judge be censured for violations of the Oregon Code of Judicial Conduct.


OVERVIEW: The commission charged that the judge had personally solicited campaign contributions through his annual golf tournament fund-raiser, had used official letterhead, his judicial assistant's work time, and other public resources for personal and campaign-related business, and had used his official position or office to influence or obtain advancement of his personal interests. In its de novo review, the court suspended the judge from office without salary for six months for numerous ethical violations. The court determined that the judge's extensive use of state resources for personal and campaign purposes and his repeated and willful use of the circuit court's official and colorful letterhead and the title of his office to add credibility to his promotion of his own interests and the interests of those close to him to obtain personal and financial advantages ran afoul of the requirement for judges to act in a manner that promoted public confidence in the integrity and impartiality of the judiciary. The court determined that the judge's conduct reflected adversely upon his character, competence, temperament, and fitness to serve as a judge.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the accused judge had violated the code of judicial conduct. The court concluded that the appropriate sanction for the circuit court judge was a six-month suspension, during which the judge would not receive the salary of his public office.

State v. Juarez-Godinez


SC S42584


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


326 Ore. 1; 942 P.2d 772; 1997 Ore. LEXIS 102


September 4, 1996, Argued and Submitted  
August 21, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 92C-21343; CA A78977. On review from the Court of Appeals. *.


*  Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Rodney W. Miller, Judge. 135 Ore. App. 591, 900 P.2d 1044 (1995).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The order of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of delivery of controlled substances (heroin, cocaine, and marijuana). The state appealed the decision of the Oregon Court of Appeals, which affirmed the order of the circuit court suppressing all evidence that the state obtained pursuant to a warrant to search the car defendant had been driving.


OVERVIEW: The court held that held that although defendant had been placed under arrest and placed in the police car for failing to show a valid driver license, he retained a possessory interest in the car which he had been driving. There was evidence that the officer interfered in a significant way with defendant's possessory interest where the officer told defendant and his companions, after the officer was denied permission to search, that another officer and his dog were coming to check the car and the officer's statements were and reasonably could have been interpreted as curtailing, by a show of authority, defendant's rights to transfer possession of, and direct the movements of, the car; the car was thus "seized." The warrantless seizure was invalid under Or. Const. art. I, § 9, where it was not justified under any exception to the warrant requirement. The evidence procured was a product of the unlawful detention where the police by means of the unlawful detention of the car were able to subject the car to a dog sniff that, in turn, was used to obtain a search warrant, and the officer's observations alone would have been insufficient to support the issuance of a search warrant.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals affirming the circuit court order suppressing evidence was affirmed. The order of the circuit court was affirmed.

The Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversed the judgment of the trial court. The defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state charged the defendants, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.015, with one count of riot. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals, which had reversed the judgment of the trial court sustaining the defendants' demurrer.

Boise Cascade Corp. v. Board of Forestry

325 Ore. 185; 935 P.2d 411; 1997 Ore. LEXIS 29

April 10, 1997, Filed

*  Appeal from Clatsop County Circuit Court, Thomas E. Edison, Judge. 131 Ore. App. 538, 886 P.2d 1033 (1994).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded to that court for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff lumber company's inverse condemnation action alleging that defendant, through its board of forestry, had unlawfully taken plaintiff's property by denying plaintiff all beneficial use of its property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff lumber company filed a proposal with defendant state's department of forestry (department) to log a 64-acre parcel of plaintiff's land. The department denied the proposal because it did not provide sufficient protection for spotted owl habitat as required by Or. Admin. R. 629-24-809. After plaintiff submitted a revised plan, the department denied plaintiff authority to log on the property except on eight acres within a prescribed time period. Plaintiff appealed the decision to the board of forestry (board), claiming that the restrictions constituted an unconstitutional "taking" under Or. Const. art. I, § 18 and U.S. Const., amend. V. After the board denied the appeal, plaintiff brought an inverse condemnation action against defendant. The circuit court dismissed the action, but the appellate court reversed the dismissal. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's order in part because the circuit court and board had concurrent jurisdiction and plaintiff's allegation that it was deprived of all economically viable use of 56 acres stated an inverse condemnation claim. The court reversed the order concerning remaining acres for which limited logging was authorized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order reversing the dismissal of plaintiff lumber company's inverse condemnation action against defendant state because the circuit court and board of forestry had concurrent jurisdiction and because plaintiff's allegation that it was deprived of all economically viable use of 56 acres of property stated an inverse condemnation claim. The court reversed the order concerning acres for which limited logging was authorized.

State ex rel. Huddleston v. Sawyer


SC S42938 *


* Relating to Jackson County Circuit Court No. 952538CC2.


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


324 Ore. 597; 932 P.2d 1145; 1997 Ore. LEXIS 9


September 9, 1996, Argued and Submitted  
February 21, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied December 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7073.


PRIOR HISTORY: Peremptory writ to issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator district attorney (DA) prosecuted defendant accused for manslaughter in the Circuit Court for Jackson County (Oregon). At sentencing, the accused argued that the sentencing statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.700, was unconstitutional. Defendant judge held that the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution. The DA sought a writ of mandamus to compel the judge to sentence the accused under § 137.700.


OVERVIEW: Section 137.700 required a 75-month minimum sentence, but the judge imposed a 20-month presumptive sentence under the sentencing guidelines. The court held that the judge erred when he refused to apply § 137.700. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandamus and required the judge to enter a corrected judgment that imposed sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.700(2)(e). The court rejected the judge's argument that mandamus was not appropriate where the state could appeal from the underlying case because the state did not have the right to appeal the accused's presumptive sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.222(4)(a) and (2)(a). The court also rejected the accused's assertions that § 137.700 violated the right of allocution, the reformation clause, and the equal privileges and immunities clause of Or. Const. art. I, §§ 11, 15, and 20, as well as the separation-of-powers of Or. Const. art. III, § 1, and art. VII, § 1. In addition the court found that the accused's claim under the Guarantee Clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 4, was not justiciable in state court. Finally, the court rejected the judge's claim that § 137.700 violated the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court directed the issuance of a peremptory writ of mandamus and required the judge to enter a corrected judgment in the underlying criminal case that imposed sentence for the crime of second-degree manslaughter in accordance with the sentencing statute.

Vannatta v. Keisling


SC S42506


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


324 Ore. 514; 931 P.2d 770; 1997 Ore. LEXIS 5


May 8, 1996, Argued and submitted  
February 6, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: An original proceeding pursuant to Oregon Laws 1995, chapter 1, section 23(1).



DISPOSITION: Sections 3, 4, 11, 14, 15, 16, and 17 of Measure 9 are declared void. The remainder of Measure 9 is not invalid on any ground urged by the petitioners in this proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners were a group that included a political action committee, a non-profit and a for-profit corporation, a lobbyist, a potential candidate, and a guardian ad litem. The group sought a declaration that 1995 Or. Laws chapter 1 (Measure 9) was unconstitutional or, alternatively, that certain sections of Measure 9 violated state constitutional protections. Respondent Secretary of State of the State of Oregon opposed the petition.


OVERVIEW: The court made the following holdings: (1) In general, contributions to political campaigns and candidates were a protected form of expression under Or. Const. art. I, § 8. (2) Or. Const. art. II, § 22, did not preempt or eliminate whatever protection art. I, § 8 afforded to campaign contributions made by individuals residing with the voting district in question. (3) Or. Const. art. II, § 8 dealt with elections themselves, and not political campaigns. (4) Portions of Measure 9 that expressly limited, or banned outright, campaign contributions that could be given to or accepted by a candidate were unconstitutional limitations of political speech protected by Or. Const. art. I, § 8 because they did not fall under an historical exception, were not targeted at a specific, identifiable harm, and did not fall under the "incompatibility" exception. Provisions dependent on the unconstitutional provisions were also void because they were "incomplete and incapable of being executed." (5) Measure 9 sections dealing with a voluntary option whereby candidates could agree to self-imposed expenditure limits were not unconstitutional. 6) The group was not entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court declared void the portions of Measure 9 that were directed at restricting the protected expression of political campaign contributions and declared them in violation of the portion of the state constitution protecting free speech. The court also voided portions of Measure 9 that were dependent upon the portions declared unconstitutional. The court held that the remainder of Measure 9 was not invalid.

State v. Moore

324 Ore. 396; 927 P.2d 1073; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 128

DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of aggravated murder, two counts of murder, one count of burglary, and one count of kidnapping in the second degree. The Circuit Court of Marion County (Oregon) convicted him of all counts and sentenced him to death. The matter came before the court on automatic and direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: The defendant argued several errors relating to both the guilt and penalty trial phases. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying the defendant's motion to suppress his post-arrest statements to police because they had complied with the requirements of Miranda and his statements were voluntary. The court held that the trial court did not err in allowing the State to use two mental health experts to rebut the defendant's affirmative defense of extreme emotional disturbance. The court reasoned that the examinations and testimony by the experts were proper because the State had a right pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 161.135(5), .315 to have at least one psychiatrist examine the defendant after his notice of affirmative defense was filed. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting evidence, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. 163.150(1)(b)(B), of the defendant's prior violent conduct and his belief in white supremacy because that evidence, taken together, was probative of the defendant's future dangerousness. The trial court properly refused to give the defendant's requested charges on jury sympathy because they were not based upon the mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in convicting the defendant and in sentencing him to death.

State v. Webb


SC S42828


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


324 Ore. 380; 927 P.2d 79; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 124


September 9, 1996, Argued and submitted  
November 29, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DC DCR93-13043. CA A83199. On review from the Court of Appeals. *.


*  Appeal from Clackamas County District Court, Alan R. Jack, Judge. 137 Ore. App. 43, 903 P.2d 393 (1995).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which ruled in favor of defendant when it reversed the judgment of the district court that convicted defendant of a misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the district court for a misdemeanor. The preceding court reversed defendant's conviction on the ground that the district court lacked subject-matter jurisdiction over the action. At the time of the offense, the crime was subject to a fine of up to $ 5,000 and defendant alleged that the district court's jurisdiction over misdemeanors was limited to cases in which the fine could not exceed $ 3,000. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the preceding court and affirmed the judgment of the district court. The court interpreted the grant of jurisdiction provided in Or. Rev. Stat. § 46.040 to intend that there were two types of jurisdiction, both independent of each other. The court determined that the limiting clause in § 46.040 that limited the district court's jurisdiction to matters where the fine did not exceed $ 3,000 applied only to the second grant of jurisdiction. The court stated that, under the first grant of jurisdiction in § 46.040, the district courts had jurisdiction over all misdemeanors, including defendant's offense. The court concluded that the district court had subject-matter jurisdiction when it convicted defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the preceding court and affirmed the judgment of the district court that convicted defendant of a misdemeanor.

Writ of certiorari denied Montez v. Oregon, 520 U.S. 1233, 117 S. Ct. 1830, 137 L. Ed. 2d 1036, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 3176 (1997)
Petition denied by Montez v. Czerniak, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 1240 (Or., Dec. 26, 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at Montez v. Czerniak, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 586 (Or., July 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC C870834702. On automatic and direct review of the sentence of death entered on remand by the Circuit Court for Multnomah County. * Kimberly C. Frankel, Judge.


*  309 Ore. 564, 789 P.2d 1352 (1990).


State v. Montez, 309 Ore. 564, 789 P.2d 1352, 1990 Ore. LEXIS 68 (1990)



DISPOSITION: The sentence of death is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court for Multnomah County (Oregon), which sentenced defendant to death on remand after a jury found him guilty of aggravated murder and related offenses.


OVERVIEW: The case was before the court for a second time on automatic and direct review of a sentence of death pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150(1)(g). Previously, a jury found that defendant had committed aggravated murder and related offenses, and he was sentenced to death. The court had affirmed defendant's convictions but vacated his sentence. On remand, the trial court empaneled a new sentencing jury. The jury answered certain question in the affirmative and, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150(1)(f), the trial judge imposed a sentence of death. Defendant appealed and requested the court to vacate his death sentence. The court concluded that none of defendant's assignments of error had merit and affirmed the sentence of death. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in permitting the state, during the second penalty-phase proceeding before a newly empaneled jury, to introduce evidence that the state had introduced previously during the guilt-phase proceeding. The court held that the trial court did not apply an ex post facto law by sentencing defendant before a new jury and by admitting evidence that was properly excluded in earlier proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that imposed a sentence of death upon defendant for committing aggravated murder and related offenses.

Mabon v. Kulongoski


SC S43562


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


324 Ore. 315; 925 P.2d 1234; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 106


September 16, 1996, Submitted on the record  
October 31, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petition to review ballot title.



DISPOSITION: Ballot title certified. This decision shall become effective in accordance with ORAP 11.30(10).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a state elector, sought review of a ballot title for a proposed initiative measure on third trimester abortions, challenging the title given the measure by respondent Oregon attorney general, in an original proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The state attorney general proposed a ballot title on a measure regarding prohibition of late trimester abortions. The title read: "Amends Constitution; bans second, third trimester abortions with one exception; permits lawsuits." The elector claimed that the caption failed reasonably to identify the subject matter of the measure, violating Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.035(2)(a). He argued that the phrase "permits lawsuits" should be deleted from the caption and the result statements. He claimed that the summary was not impartial and sought to replace "pregnant woman" with "mother." The court noted that the proposed measure: (1) prohibited second and third trimester abortions except when necessary to save the life of the pregnant woman; (2) required enabling legislation be enacted immediately; and (3) gave every Oregon resident and non-profit entity doing business in the state standing to initiate litigation for enforcement. It also noted that the issues of when life begins or when someone becomes a mother were not being decided. The ballot title complied with statute. The court certified the title to the secretary of state.


OUTCOME: The ballot title was certified. The elector was entitled to seek a different title and his arguments were consistent with those made during the administrative process. But the attorney general's caption, "yes vote" and "no vote" result statements, and summary all substantially complied with statutory requirements.

Stovall v. State by & Through Oregon DOT


SC S43012

* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Jamese Rhoades, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of the circuit court are reversed. The cases are remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and retired employees, sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which rendered judgment against the state, enjoined the state from taxing the employees' Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS) benefits, and enjoined the state from seeking funds from respondent local employers.


OVERVIEW: In a previous action, it was determined that it was a breach of contract for the state to subject the retired employees' pension benefits to state income taxes paid under the Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS). The retired employees afterwards filed suit against the state and the local employers for breach of contract. The trial court held that the state was liable for those damages, enjoined the state from seeking contribution from local employers, and enjoined the implementation of legislative enactments intended to compensate the retired employees for the damages suffered. On appeal, the court reversed and held that a state contract would not be inferred from legislation that did not unambiguously express an intention to create a contract. In addition, the court held that a court would not imply the existence of a statutory contract between the state and another party.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against the state.

State v. Cookman


SC S41424


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


324 Ore. 19; 920 P.2d 1086; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 81


January 12, 1995, Argued and submitted  
August 15, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 91-1524; CA A73459. On review from the Court of Appeals.*


*  Appeal from Clackamas County Circuit Court, Charles A. Sams, Judge. 127 Ore. App. 283, 873 P.2d 335 (1994).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the order of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state petitioned for review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the trial court's grant of defendant's demurrer and its dismissal of the indictment charging defendant with using a child in a display of sexually explicit conduct, dealing in depictions of a child's sexual conduct, and sexual abuse in the first degree, on the grounds that the prosecution was untimely under Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.125 (1985).


OVERVIEW: In October, 1991, the warrant was issued for defendant's arrest on the crimes charged, which alleged occurred between June and September, 1986. Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.125 (1985), which was in effect at the time defendant allegedly committed the crimes, established a three-year statute of limitations for prosecution of those crimes. That statute was amended in 1989 to extend the limitations period to six years, and in 1991 to extend the limitations period for certain sex crimes involving children. In the 1991 amendment, the legislature stated that the amendments applied to revive any cause of action barred under the 1989 version of § 131.125. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the indictment. The court first held that the 1991 revival also applied to actions barred under the pre-1989 version of § 131.125. The court held that the state constitution's ex post facto provision, Or. Const. art. I, § 21, prohibited the retroactive application of an amended criminal statute of limitations, extending the period of limitations, to revive prosecutions that already were time-barred when the amendment took effect, because such revival would deprive a defendant of an absolute defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court that affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the indictment against defendant.

 

35 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stoneman


SC S42085


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


323 Ore. 536; 920 P.2d 535; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 71


November 9, 1995, Argued and submitted  
July 18, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 90-12-5153-C; CA A70085. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Malheur County Circuit Court, F. J. Yraguen, Judge. 132 Ore. App. 137, 888 P.2d 39 (1994).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of the judgment from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining defendant's demurrer on the grounds that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.680 (1987) was unconstitutional. Defendant had been charged with purchasing a magazine and a video containing portrayals of sexually explicit conduct by a child known by defendant to be under 18 years of age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 163.680 was unconstitutional because it restricted freedom of expression in violation of Or. Const. art. 1, § 8. The appellate court found that the statute was an invalid content-driven restriction on speech. On appeal, the court determined that of the two categories of statutes, those that focus on the content of speech and those that focus of the effect of speech, § 163.680 focused on the effect of the speech. The court concluded that § 163.680 prohibited the purchase of visual reproductions of sexually explicit conduct by a child under the age of 18, not in terms of the content of the reproductions, but because the reproductions owe their existence to the commission of sexual abuse of a child and provide an economic incentive to abuse the child. The court found that the state's authority to protect children included the authority to destroy the incentives for causing that harm. The court held that Or. Const. art. I, § 8 did not prohibit a statute which protected children from sexual exploitation, even when the exploitation was shared with others through a communicative device, and that § 163.680 was a constitutionally valid prohibition.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed. The action was remanded to the trial court for further action.

Kilminster v. Day Mgmt. Corp.


SC S42217


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


323 Ore. 618; 919 P.2d 474; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 70


January 10, 1996, Argued and submitted  
July 18, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 9301-00574; CA A82220. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


*  Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Nely M. Johnson, Judge. 133 Ore. App. 159, 890 P.2d 1004 (1995).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimants, parents of decedent, challenged the decision from the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon), which granted summary judgment to defendant employer for parents' claims alleging negligent wrongful death, intentional wrongful death, and violation of the Oregon Racketeer Influenced Corrupt Organization Act (ORICO), Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 166.715 to 166.735. The circuit court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.018 barred parents' actions.


OVERVIEW: The parents contended that the exclusivity provision of the Workers' Compensation Act, specifically Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.018, did not preclude a wrongful death claim brought under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.020. The court held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.020 gave parents, as decedent's representatives, a derivative right to maintain an action if the decedent could have maintained an action but held that they did not have an independent basis from which to derive such a right. The court held that because there was no state common law action for wrongful death based on negligence, the parents suffered no legally cognizable injury to their person. The court also held that § 656.018 barred the parents' ORICO claim. However, the court held that the parents alleged facts sufficient to meet the deliberate intent to injure standards established in Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.156(2) because they alleged that the employer knew that decedent, or someone like him, would be injured from a fall from the tower and that the employer decided to forego taking safety procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the negligent wrongful death and ORICO claims. The judgment was reversed and remanded as to the intentional wrongful death claim.

State v. Kitzman


SC S41724, S41793 (consolidated for argument and opinion)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


323 Ore. 589; 920 P.2d 134; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 68


May 5, 1995, Argued and submitted  
July 18, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 922182; CA A77967. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


*  Appeal from Lincoln County Circuit Court, Charles P. Littlehales, Judge. 129 Ore. App. 520, 879 P.2d 1326 (1994).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed his conviction for sexual assault of two children but affirmed the conviction as to the oldest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for 14 counts of sexual abuse involving three children, and a hearing was held to determine whether the two younger children were competent and available to testify at trial. Defendant was not permitted to be present at the hearing and his attorney was not allowed to examine them, per the trial court's interpretation of Or. Evid. Code 803(18a)(b) (1991). The trial court ruled that the children were unavailable to testify, but their out of court statements were admissible. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. The conviction was affirmed as to the oldest child, but reversed on the two younger ones, and defendant sought review. The court reversed all convictions because defendant should have been allowed to be present at the hearing. It was a violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 11 to exclude defendant from the hearing and to preclude his lawyer from examining the children. Inquiry as to any unwillingness to testify may have disclosed either an improper influence on the witness by the prosecution or the child's mother or, alternatively, eventually may have disclosed a willingness on the part of the witness to communicate about some of the events at issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed all the convictions against defendant for sexual abuse of the three children because the trial court should have allowed him to attend the pretrial hearing on competency and availability and should have allowed his attorney to examine the children.

Oregon State Police Officers' Ass'n v. State


SC S42333 (Control), SC S42511, SC S42355


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


323 Ore. 356; 918 P.2d 765; 1996 Ore. LEXIS 54


October 25, 1995, Argued and submitted  
June 21, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 94C-14019; CC 94C-13963; 94-12-08563; CC 95-C10338. On certification from the Court of Appeals pursuant to Oregon Laws 1995, chapter 284. *


* Appeals from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Stephen S. Walker, Judge, and Marion County Circuit Court, Richard D. Barber, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of the circuit courts in OSPOA, Tissue, and SPEU are affirmed. The judgment in Morgan on the City of Portland's cross-claim is reversed and is remanded to the circuit court for entry of a judgment for the State of Oregon on the City's cross-claim; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state sought review of orders by the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon), which granted summary judgment to plaintiff state employees and ruled that Or. Const. art. IX, §§ 10, 11, 12 violated the Contracts Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, because such sections interfered with plaintiffs' Public Employee Retirement System contract with defendant by altering the terms of the contract after employment had started.


OVERVIEW: Or. Const. art. IX was amended and approved by voters, adding Or. Const. art. IX §§ 10, 11, 12, 13. Such sections had the effect of altering the Public Employees' Retirement System (PERS). Plaintiff public employees filed suit against defendant state, claiming that the enactment of the amendments violated the Contracts Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and arguing that defendant had entered into contractual relations with them, that defendant's PERS obligations vested when plaintiffs accepted or continued employment, and that such obligations could not be modified or terminated. The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, ruling that Or. Const. art. IX, §§ 10, 11, 12 violated the Contracts Clause and were unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that contractual relations between an annuitant and an employer were created when an annuitant made a contribution to a pension fund, and upon full performance, rights accrued which could not be impaired by subsequent legislation. An employee who accepted an initial retirement plan offer had vested contract rights which could not be altered by a second plan put into effect after the initial plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that constitutional amendments which altered plaintiff public employees' retirement system contract with defendant state violated the federal Contracts Clause and were void. Contractual relations between an annuitant and an employer were created when the annuitant made contributions to a pension fund, and such relations could not be impaired by subsequent legislation.
