Lincoln Loan Co. v. City of Portland


SC No. S38335


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


317 Ore. 192; 855 P.2d 151; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 100


March 5, 1992, Argued and submitted  
July 22, 1993, Decided  
July 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. A8810-05939; CA No. A65509.


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Arthur M. LaFrance, Judge pro tempore. 107 Or App 784, 813 P2d 1139 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are reversed. This case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner house owner sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals of Oregon, which affirmed the circuit court's order denying a petition for writ of review of respondent city's decision to demolish the house owner's vacant residential structure.


OVERVIEW: The house owner was served with a complaint charging it with maintaining a building with city code violations. At a subsequent hearing, the city only sought demolition of the building and a civil penalty, it did not seek to have the building repaired to eliminate the code violations. The house owner did not apply for a demolition permit and the city demolished the building, pursuant to Portland, Or., City Code § 22.05.010(a). The circuit court denied the house owner's petition for writ of review of the city's decision. The court of appeals affirmed. The court reversed the decisions of the circuit court and the court of appeals because the city's hearing officer misconstrued his authority under § 22.05.010(a) by ordering the demolition of the building without first having made any finding as to why demolition was a reasonable choice, as required by Portland, Or., City Code § 22.03.110(b).Therefore, it was error for the circuit court to deny the writ if it appeared that improperly construing the city code was to the injury of some substantial interest of the homeowner. The case was remanded to circuit court for the fashioning of a remedy, if any, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.100.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the court of appeals and the circuit court that denied a petition for writ of review of the city's decision to demolish the house owner's vacant residential structure. The case was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Stevens v. City of Cannon Beach


SC No. S39585


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


317 Ore. 131; 854 P.2d 449; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 94; 24 ELR 20913

July 1, 1993, Decided  
July 1, 1993, Filed

* Appeal from Clatsop County Circuit Court, Thomas E. Edison, Judge. 114 Or App 457, 835 P2d 940 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought an action against defendant city for inverse condemnation under Or. Const. art. 1, § 8 and U.S. Const. amend. V, alleging that the Cannon Beach, Or., Zoning Ordinance 79-4A was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) affirmed the dismissal. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners applied to the city for permits to build a privacy sea wall as a part of a development of oceanfront land for eventual motel or hotel use. The city denied the application. The trial court dismissed the landowners' complaint for failure to state a cause of action. On appeal, the landowner claimed that the trial court improperly applied case law retroactively to cancel all development rights of private owners. OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the city upholding the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance was affirmed.

State v. Graf


SC No. S39638


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 544; 853 P.2d 277; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 81


March 4, 1993, Argued and submitted  
June 17, 1993, Decided  
June 17, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC Nos. 900633472, 900633473, 900633474; CA No. A69280.


*  Appeal from Union County Circuit Court, Ronald D. Schenck, Judge. 114 Or App 275, 835 P2d 934 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed on different grounds. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed a decision dismissing charges filed against him for crimes that allegedly occurred during his employment with the Oregon Department of Transportation (Department).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with crimes that occurred during his employment. He successfully claimed that the Department coerced him into testifying at a pre-termination hearing, and he was entitled to transactional immunity and dismissal of some of the criminal charges. The appellate court reversed the decision, stating that defendant was compelled to testify within the meaning of Or. Const. art. I, § 12 and the Fifth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The appellate court also found that in the absence of a statutory grant of immunity, the employee could simply suppress his testimony before the Department and any evidence derived therefrom. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the appellate court but on different grounds. The court held that Or. Admin. R. 105-80-0003(3) exerted no compulsion on defendant to testify at the pre-termination hearing because he was not required to testify. The rule specified that silence did not constitute any admission to the charges. Therefore, the court found that the transactional immunity question was not an issue because there was no unconstitutionally compelled testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Nielsen


SC No. S37614


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 611; 853 P.2d 256; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 85


April 2, 1991, Argued and submitted  
June 17, 1993, Decided  
June 17, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. C89-0964CR; CA No. A62544.


* Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, John B. Lewis, Judge. 103 Or App 486, 798 P2d 269 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sough review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed his conviction for forgery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with forgery and during his trial, the court admitted over his objection, the out-of-court statements of defendant's accomplice. Defendant was convicted and sought review of the lower court's affirmance of his conviction. He contended that the statements did not meet the requirements of Or. Evid. Code 804(1)(e) and Or. Evid. Code 804(3)(c) and that the admission of the statement violated his rights to confrontation under Or. Const. art. I, § 11 and U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for forgery. The accomplice's hearsay statement was properly admitted because the state showed that the accomplice was unavailable and because the state had attempted to obtain the declarant by process or other reasonable means. The state showed that the statement was trustworthy because the statement was made against penal interest. The statement did not violate defendant's right to confront witnesses against him under the state and federal constitutions because the declarant was shown to be unavailable and because the statement had an adequate indicia of reliability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's forgery conviction.

State v. Dameron


SC No. S37145


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 448; 853 P.2d 1285; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 67


March 6, 1992, Argued and submitted; February 4 1993 and April 8, 1993, Reassigned  
May 28, 1993, Decided  
May 28, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * DC No. D881992M; CA No. A60258.


* Appeal from Washington County District Court, Mark Gardner, Judge. 101 Or App 237, 789 P2d 707 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed on different grounds. The judgment of the district court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversed defendant's conviction for trespass in the second degree, which was in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.245. The State appealed the reversal. The Court of Appeals held that defendant had established at trial that he was engaged in a constitutionally protected activity of gathering signatures for an initiative petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was gathering signatures for an initiative petition on a privately owned sidewalk outside an entrance to a store located in a shopping center. When defendant refused to leave, after being directed to by the person in charge of the store, defendant was arrested for trespassing. The court decided the case on a narrow and subconstitutional ground. The court decided that the State failed to prove that it was almost certainly true that defendant was lawfully directed to leave the premises and, therefore, that he remained unlawfully on the premises within the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 164.245(1), 164.205(3)(b). No rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that he remained unlawfully on the premises. If defendant had a legal right to remain, then he was not lawfully directed to leave. The conviction was reversed for failure of proof. The case did not involve reasonable time, place, and manner restrictions. In most cases, the State would have met its burden of proving that defendant remained unlawfully by showing that defendant failed to leave. However, the State did not prove, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant remained unlawfully.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of defendant's conviction for trespassing, but on different grounds.

 

86 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Carrier v. Hicks


SC No. S37366


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 341; 851 P.2d 581; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 59


November 7, 1990, Argued and submitted; April 13, 1993, Reassigned  
May 21, 1993, Decided  
May 21, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 87-2112; CA No. A60563.


* Appeal from the Columbia County Circuit Court, Donald Kalberer, Judge. 102 Or App 13, 793 P2d 329 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent claimant filed a complaint against petitioner insureds to recover for personal injuries. The insureds' insurer became insolvent and the Oregon Insurance Guaranty Association (OIGA) succeeded to the defense. The claimant filed an uninsured motorist claim and was awarded less than his policy limits. The circuit court granted the insureds' motion for summary judgment. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversed. The insureds appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether an uninsured motorist claimant was required to exhaust all other insurance coverage before recovering from either the insureds whose liability insurer was insolvent or from the OIGA, which succeeded to the insolvent insurer's claims. The court held that, under the requirements of Or. Rev. Stat. § 734.640(1), the limits of any other applicable policy had to be exhausted before the claimant could assert a claim to recover damages covered by the OIGA plan against the insureds or against OIGA. If the recovery under his uninsured motorist (UM) or underinsured motorist (UIM) coverage was less than UM/UIM policy limits, the lesser amount was all that the claimant was legally entitled to receive under Or. Rev. Stat. § 742.504(10). Because the claimant received the award of damages to which he was legally entitled, and that award did not exhaust the limits of his UM and UIM coverage, he was nonetheless foreclosed from further pursuing his claim against the insureds or OIGA to recover damages covered by the OIGA plan. The court held that the OIGA law and the UM/UIM law governing arbitration did not violate the claimant's Or. Const. art. I, § 17 right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals overturning the insureds' summary judgment, and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

The court that it was proven that the offense was committed in an occupied dwelling according to the offense subcategory for first-degree burglary under § 164.225, and that therefore, the circuit court did not err in sentencing defendant accordingly.

Oberg v. Honda Motor Co.


SC No. S38436


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 263; 851 P.2d 1084; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 62; 61 U.S.L.W. 2743; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,548


January 10, 1992, Argued and submitted; March 30, 1993, Reassigned  
May 20, 1993, Decided  
May 20, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 27, 1993. Opinion on Remand from Supreme Court of United States February 2, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ore. LEXIS 2.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. A8709-05897; CA No. A61587.


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Robert P. Jones, Judge. 108 Or App 43, 814 P2d 517 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, manufacturers and sellers, appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon) that affirmed a judgment in favor of plaintiff consumer in his products liability action.


OVERVIEW: A consumer attempted to drive an all-terrain vehicle (ATV) up a steep embankment. It overturned backward and injured him. A jury returned a verdict in favor of the consumer in his subsequent product liability action against the manufacturers and sellers. The appellate court affirmed. On further appeal, the court affirmed. Consumer Products Safety Commission documents were relevant to issues at trial and were not hearsay because they were offered to prove notice of the dangerousness of ATVs, not the truth of the matters asserted therein. The provision against excessive fines in Or. Const. art. I, § 16 applied only to criminal cases. Application of objective criteria in considering punitive damages ensured that sufficiently definite and meaningful constraints were imposed on the finder of fact. The criteria established by Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.925 were detailed and objective, and were thus constitutionally sufficient. The jury was instructed properly about the substantive criteria to be applied, and there was evidence to support its determination. The punitive damages award thus did not violate the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of a consumer in his products liability action against manufacturers and sellers of an all-terrain vehicle. The admission of Consumer Products Safety Commission documents was not error, a state constitutional provision against excessive fines applied only to criminal cases, and the procedure for arriving at the punitive damages award was constitutionally sound.

Portland v. Jackson


SC No. S39063


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 143; 850 P.2d 1093; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 48


September 4, 1992, Argued and submitted  
April 29, 1993, Decided  
April 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * DC DA No. 396491-8906; CA No. A64089.


*  Appeal from Multnomah County District Court, Anthony L. Casciato, Judge. 111 Or App 233, 826 P2d 37 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the district court are reversed. The case is remanded to the district court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the decision of the trial court, which sustained the demurrer of defendant and dismissed the action against defendant for the crime of indecent exposure under the Portland, Or., City Code § 14.24.060.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the crime of indecent exposure under § 14.24.060, which did not require a culpable mental state. Defendant demurred, claiming that because the state public indecency statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.465, required a culpable mental state, the ordinance was invalid because it was in conflict with the statute. The trial court sustained the demurrer and dismissed the action. The court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the repeal of former Or. Rev. Stat. § 167.145, without more, did not establish a legislative political decision to permit non-sexually motivated public nudity. In the absence of stronger evidence of legislative intent, the court was unconvinced that the legislature intended to permit the conduct prohibited in the city ordinance. Therefore, the city's "indecent exposure" ordinance did not conflict with the state "public indecency" statute, and the ordinance was valid under Or. Const. art. XI, § 2.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the court of appeals, which affirmed the decision of the trial court, which sustained the demurrer of defendant and dismissed the action against defendant for the crime of indecent exposure under a city ordinance.

Gilliam County v. Department of Envtl. Quality


SC Nos. S39659, S39658 (Cases consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 99; 849 P.2d 500; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 46; 24 ELR 20065


March 4, 1993, Argued and submitted  
April 15, 1993, Decided  
April 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Granted September 28, 1993 to the United States Supreme Court. Opinion of April 4, 1994, Reported at: 1994 U.S. LEXIS 2659. Opinion on Remand June 30, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ore. LEXIS 58.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * DEQ No. 45-1990; CA Nos. A68441 (Control), A68455.


*  Judicial review from the Department of Environmental Quality and the Environmental Quality Commission. 114 Or App 369, 837 P2d 965 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, solid waste companies and county, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which ruled generally in favor of respondent, department of environmental quality as to the validity of Or. Admin. R. 340-61-115(1), Or. Admin. R. 340-61-120(6), and Or. Rev. Stat. § 459.298. At issue was the validity of regulations imposing a per-ton surcharge on the disposal in Oregon of solid waste generated outside the state.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals concluded that the portions of Or. Rev. Stat. § 459.298 relating to the approval of the surcharge by the emergency board and joint committee on ways and means was unconstitutional, but severable. The court of appeals also held that Or. Admin. R. 340-61-115(1) and Or. Admin. R. 340-61-120(6) did not violate the commerce clause because the surcharge imposed on out-of-state waste was a permissible compensatory fee for specific costs incurred by the state. The court affirmed. As did the court of appeals, the court concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. 459.298 was unconstitutional in that it impermissibly required approval of the surcharge by the emergency board and by the joint committee on ways and means. The court found those portions severable, however, and deleted them from the statute, while keeping the remaining portions in force. The court further concluded that the surcharge did not, on its face, constitute discrimination against interstate commerce in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3 because of the express nexus to actual costs incurred. There was a discernible basis for the surcharge apart from that origin.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals declaring certain portions of regulations imposing a surcharge on solid waste disposal unconstitutional and severing those portions, but upholding the validity of the other regulations at issue.

 

92 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


SC No. S37304 (Cases Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


316 Ore. 6; 848 P.2d 599; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 43


October 9, 1990, Argued and submitted  
April 8, 1993, Decided  
April 8, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 87030467; CA Nos. A47434 (Control), A47437.


*  Appeal from Linn County Circuit Court, William O. Lewis, Judge. 101 Or App 281, 790 P2d 1152 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgments of the circuit court are reversed. The cases are remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were separately indicted on drug-related offenses, their motions to suppress evidence seized pursuant to a search warrant were denied, and they were convicted by the circuit court. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) consolidated the cases and affirmed the judgments. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The search warrant was issued on the basis of an officer's affidavit, which reported on his warrantless police observation of the interior of defendants' residence. The officer swore that he saw green plants when he looked through the windows into defendants' house, that the color and a plant stem were consistent with marijuana, and that he was both trained and experienced in visual identification of growing marijuana. The court found that the officer did not state at any point that plants he saw were marijuana or that he believed they were marijuana. The court reversed and remanded because the officer's affidavit did not allege sufficient particularized facts to establish probable cause to search as required by statute for a warrant to intrude on defendants' constitutionally protected privacy interests. The affidavit omitted any conclusion drawn as to the nature of the green plants observed and alleged insufficient information to support a conclusion that the plants were marijuana. Because no valid warrant supported the search, the search was an unauthorized one and the evidence seized should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court decision that affirmed defendants' judgments of conviction, reversed the judgments of conviction by the circuit court, and remanded the cases to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

93 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boots


SC No. S39368


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 572; 848 P.2d 76; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 36


November 4, 1992, Argued and submitted  
March 25, 1993, Decided  
March 25, 1993, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 25, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 10-86-07965; CA No. A67325.


* Appeal from Lane County Circuit Court, Jack L. Mattison, Judge. 112 Or App 25, 826 P2d 1049 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is modified. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated murder following a limited retrial after remand. The appellate court ruled that in limiting the jury's instructions to the existence of the aggravating factor, the trial court violated the remand order.


OVERVIEW: Although his murder conviction stood, defendant's conviction for aggravated murder was retried under a remand order and he was convicted again. The appellate court reversed the conviction, ruling that the trial court violated the remand order. In its petition for review, the state asserted that the remand order did not require a complete retrial of all elements of the aggravated murder charge. The court modified the appellate court decision, reversed the trial court judgment, and remanded the case again, agreeing that a limited retrial was permissible. It did not violate defendant's right not to be put in double jeopardy, his right to a trial by jury, or his right to be presumed innocent. The trial court erred, however, in its jury instructions. In the first trial it was possible that the jury found that defendant murdered to conceal the identity of a robber other than himself. Under that scenario, defendant would have been guilty of aggravated murder without having committed the robbery. The trial court, therefore, erred here in instructing the jury that defendant had committed first degree robbery. The court also ruled that the error prejudiced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decision of the appellate court. The court also reversed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of aggravated murder in the remand trial, and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

Pendell v. Department of Revenue


SC No. S39418


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 608; 847 P.2d 846; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 30


January 7, 1993, Argued and submitted  
March 25, 1993, Decided  
March 25, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. * Carl N. Byers, Judge. OTC No. 3150.


*  12 OTR 204 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Oregon Tax Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the judgment of the Oregon Tax Court, which set aside respondent Department of Revenue's order and remanded the case to the Department of Revenue with instructions to provide the taxpayers with a refund, without interest for excess taxes paid on federal retirement income. On appeal, the taxpayers claimed that they were entitled to interest and attorney's fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, federal retirees who paid state income taxes on their federal pensions under protest, filed an action in state tax court to obtain a refund, plus interest. The Department of Revenue (DOR) asserted that, in view of the court decision invalidating the state tax law that taxed federal retirement income while exempting state retirement income, the taxpayers were entitled to a refund, but they were not entitled to interest. The tax court ordered refund without interest and declined to award the taxpayers costs or attorney's fees. The taxpayers appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the tax court's decision and declined to award costs and attorney's fees on the appeal. The court held that Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 305.770 to 305.785 were self-contained statutes that allowed for interest in one situation only, and that the taxpayers did not qualify under that situation. The court rejected the taxpayers' claim that they were entitled to an award of interest for constitutional reasons. The court also found that the tax court had not abused its discretion by declining to award the taxpayers, who had appeared pro se, attorney's fees pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 305.490(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's decision, which awarded the taxpayers a refund without interest and that declined to award costs or attorney's fees to the taxpayers. The court also declined to award costs or attorney's fees on the appeal.

 

95 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Lloyd Corp. v. Whiffen


SC No. S38606


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 500; 849 P.2d 446; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 34


March 3, 1992, Argued and submitted  
March 23, 1993, Decided  
March 23, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * Reassigned February 4, 1993, to Tongue, retired Justice, pro tempore. CC Nos. A8512-08127, A8803-01216; CA No. A62648.


* Appeal from order of the Multnomah County Circuit Court, Kristena A. LaMar, Judge. 107 Or App 773, 813 P2d 573 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Rules 1, 2, 5 and 15 of the circuit court's injunction are stricken. The balance of the circuit court's injunction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shopping center sought an injunction from the trial court to enjoin defendant signature solicitors (solicitors) from doing anything not in accordance with shopping center rules. The trial court granted the injunction. Solicitors appealed. The Court of appeals affirmed the trial court's decision. Solicitors sought review.


OVERVIEW: Solicitors contended that the time, place, and manner restrictions in the rules adopted by shopping center violated either Or. Const. Art. IV, §1 or Or. Cost. Art I, § 8 and the U. S. Const. amend. V and XIV. The court found that there was no taking in this case. Furthermore, the court found that shopping center's rights to free expression were not infringed by the activities of solicitor. The court determined that seeking signatures on initiative petitions was essential to the purposes of Or. Const. Art. IV, § 1. The court held that to prohibit the gathering of signatures in the common areas of shopping center impinged on the constitutional rights of solicitors. Such rights, however, were subject to reasonable time, place, and manner restrictions. The court found shopping center's rules requiring 24-hour written notice prior to solicitation, limiting the number of signature gatherers, and denying permission during certain holidays were not reasonable time, place and manner restrictions. Therefore, the court ordered these stricken from the trial court's injunction.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the following provisions be stricken from the trial court's injunction: shopping center's rules requiring 24-hour written notice prior to solicitation, limiting the number of signature gatherers, and denying permission during certain holidays. The court affirmed the remaining provisions of the trial court's injunction.

State ex rel. Mikkelsen v. Hill


SC No. S38446


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 452; 847 P.2d 402; 1993 Ore. LEXIS 23


March 2, 1992, Argued and submitted  
March 4, 1993, Decided  
March 4, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 89-11-9705-E; CA No. A66027.


*  Appeal from Harney County Circuit Court, F. J. Yraguen, Judge. 108 Or App 135, 813 P2d 1130 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Oregon Court of Appeals, which reversed on federal constitutional grounds a circuit court judgment that held defendant in criminal contempt for failure to make child support payments to relator.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the state contempt statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 33.010(1)(e), could not constitutionally require defendant affirmatively to show an inability to comply with the order to pay child support as part of establishing the requisite willfulness of criminal contempt. The court of appeals determined that the state was required to prove ability to comply with the child support order in order to establish willfulness. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and reinstated the circuit court's criminal contempt judgment. The court construed § 33.010(1)(e) as imposing upon defendant the burden of going forward with an affirmative defense that he did not have the ability to comply with the child support order. The court also held that the statutory procedure was constitutionally permissible because it remained the state's burden to prove that defendant's failure to pay support constituted contempt. The court found that the state proved its case beyond a reasonable doubt by establishing that there was a valid support order, that defendant had notice of the order, and that defendant had neither paid nor sought a modification of the order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that reversed the circuit court's judgment of criminal contempt. The court affirmed the circuit court's criminal contempt judgment.

Rev. Stat. § 759.290 was unconstitutional.

February 11, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 20, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: On automatic and direct review of the judgments of conviction and sentences of death imposed by the Circuit Court for Polk County. Rodney W. Miller, Judge. CC No. 87P-3440.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of conviction are affirmed. The sentences for robbery and burglary are vacated. The sentences of death are vacated, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Oregon) that convicted him of 10 counts of aggravated murder, two counts of robbery and one count of burglary in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for aggravated murder, robbery and burglary. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but vacated his sentences for robbery in the first degree and burglary in the first degree. The court found that the state conceded that the trial court erred in imposing separate sentences for the robbery and burglary convictions because robbery and burglary were lesser included offenses of aggravated felony murder. The court also found that defendant correctly argued and the state conceded that the trial court gave instructions to the jury in the penalty phase that unconstitutionally limited the way in which the jury could consider mitigating evidence about him. The court concluded that recent case law required that the jury be instructed that it could consider and give effect to defendant's mitigating circumstances in imposing its sentence. Therefore, the court also vacated defendant's sentence of death and remanded the case to the trial court for a new penalty-phase proceeding or, at the election of the district attorney, for entry of a sentence of life imprisonment. The court rejected defendant's other numerous claims of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated murder, robbery and burglary but vacated the sentences for robbery and burglary as lesser-included offenses. The court also vacated defendant's death sentences and remanded to the trial court for new sentencing proceedings to allow the jury to consider defendant's mitigating evidence in imposing sentence, or for entry of a sentence of life imprisonment at the district attorney's election.

State v. Ferrell


SC Nos. S38980, S39000, S39001, S39002, S39003, S39004, S39005, S39006, S39007, S39008, S39009, S39010, S39011 (Cases Consolidated for Argument and Decision)

November 5, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 31, 1992, Decided  
December 31, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC Nos. C900614CR, 9004-0603, C901331CR, 90CR2534, 90CR-1021, 90CR2527, C901396CR, C9004-32514, 90-12-36926, C90-02-31052, 90CR2288, 90CR2108, 90CR2477, 90C-20570, 90C-20631; CA Nos. A69384, A66562, A68066, A67816, A66771, A68397, A68313, A66539, A68759, A65067, A67678, A67549, A65867 (Control), A65868.


*  (S38980) Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Michael McElligott, Judge. State v. Ferrell, 111 Or App 120, 822 P2d 1212 (1992).

(S39004) Appeal from Coos County Circuit Court, Robert F. Walberg, Judge. State v. Martsch, 111 Or App 129, 822 P2d 759 (1992).

(S39005) Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Jon B. Lund, Judge. State v. Sutphin, 111 Or App 125, 822 P2d 758 (1992).

(S39006) Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Dorothy M. Baker pro tempore, Judge. State v. Sanchez-Bustamante, 111 Or App 118, 822 P2d 1211 (1992).

(S39007) Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Nely L. Johnson, Judge. State v. Thompson, 111 Or App 119, 822 P2d 1212 (1992).

(S39008) Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Kimberly C. Frankel, Judge. State v. Johnson, 111 Or App 131, 822 P2d 760 (1992).

(S39009) Appeal from Coos County Circuit Court, Richard L. Barron, Judge. State v. Guido, 111 Or App 132, 822 P2d 760 (1992).

(S39010) Appeal from Coos County Circuit Court, Richard L. Barron, Judge. State v. Fuller, 111 Or App 130, 822 P2d 760 (1992).

(S39011) Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Val D. Sloper, Judge. State v. Ramirez-Silva, 111 Or App 124, 822 P2d 757 (1992).

 [***2]



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the Court of Appeals are reversed. The judgments of conviction are affirmed and the cases are remanded to the circuit courts for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State appealed judgments of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed the convictions of 13 defendants in unrelated cases for either manufacture, delivery, or possession of controlled substances under Or. Rev. Stat. § 745.992(1) and (4), where indictments alleged a drug cultivation, manufacture, or delivery "scheme or network" under Or. Admin. R. 253-04-002, and which remanded the cases with instructions to dismiss the indictments.


OVERVIEW: The lower appellate court held in an earlier decision that the words "scheme or network" in Or. Admin. R. 253-04-002, app. 4 were unconstitutionally vague in violation of Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20 and 21. Defendants' cases were consolidated for review for a determination of whether defendants were entitled to a vacation of their convictions and a remand to trial courts with instructions for dismissal of their indictments or to affirmation of their convictions for the underlying drug offenses and a remand to trial courts for resentencing. The court held that: (1) errors in defendants' indictments did not affect the sufficiency of the remaining allegations that charged defendants with underlying drug offenses which were properly alleged; (2) the only function of the "scheme or network" allegation in each indictment was to move up the underlying drug offenses on the "crime-seriousness" scale for sentencing purposes; and (3) where a defect related to an allegation did not affect the validity of the conviction on any properly alleged underlying offense, the appropriate remedy was to affirm the conviction on the underlying offense and remand for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's judgments as to all 13 defendants, affirmed the circuit courts' judgments that convicted each defendant on underlying offenses, and remanded the cases to the respective trial courts for entry of judgments of conviction on the underlying drug offenses and for resentencing.

 

101 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Kafoury v. Jones


SC No. S39395


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 201; 843 P.2d 932; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 249


November 2, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 31, 1992, Decided  
December 31, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding in mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ to issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney filed a mandamus action asserting that defendant judge applied the wrong legal standard when he denied the attorney's motion to disqualify another judge. The motion was filed pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.250 and Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.260(1).


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed a motion to disqualify the a judge and the judge challenged the good faith of the attorney in filing the motion. A hearing was held before defendant judge and the motion was denied. The court granted an peremptory writ of mandamus directing defendant judge to grant the motion. The court held: (1) the issue to be resolved in hearing under Or. Rev. Stat. § 14-260 is whether the moving party filed the motion to disqualify in bad faith or for purposes of delay, if not, the motion must be granted; (2) the moving party is not required to show actual prejudice; (3) for purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.260(1), a motion to disqualify is made in "bad faith" if the primary aim of the motion is something other than the procurement of the fair adjudication of the action in which the motion is made; (4) § 14.260(1) does not violate Or. Const. art. VII, § 1; and (5) there was no evidence that the attorney's motion to disqualify was made in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandamus directing defendant judge to grant the motion to disqualify the other judge.

 

102 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


AFSCME Local 2623 v. Department of Corrections


SC No. S38764


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 74; 843 P.2d 409; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 237


May 8, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 24, 1992, Decided  
December 24, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CA No. A62602.


*  Judicial review of a rule of the Department of Corrections. 109 Or App 662, 820 P2d 892 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in the respects addressed in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A union representative challenged the decision from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which held that department rules permitting the department to ask employees to submit, under specified conditions, to a search of their person and possessions pursuant to Or. Admin. R. 291-41-005 to 291-41-045 were valid.


OVERVIEW: The department promulgated rules permitting it to ask employees to submit, under certain specified circumstances, to a search of their person and possessions. Or. Admin. R. 291-41-005 to 291-41-045. Union representatives challenged the rules under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.400, but the lower court held that the rules were valid. On appeal, the representatives argued that the rules violated their constitutional rights under the Or. Const. art. I, § 9, which protected them from unreasonable search or seizure, and that the department had no statutory authority to promulgate the rules. The court found that the department had statutory authority to regulate, and found that the searches did not violate any constitutional rights. However, the court declined to decide whether it would have been legally permissible to discipline an employee for refusing to consent to a search, or whether personal property located on department grounds but outside of a secure facility was subject to search. Therefore, the court only affirmed as to the respects addressed in the opinion.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was affirmed in that the department was found to be within its rights to promulgate rules requiring that employees consent to be searched.

 

103 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Long


SC No. S38896


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


315 Ore. 95; 843 P.2d 420; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 239


September 1, 1992, Argued and submitted  
December 24, 1992, Decided  
December 24, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 10-90-00555; CA No. A65593.


*  Appeal from Lane County Circuit Court, Pierre L. Van Rysselberghe, Judge. 109 Or App 221, 818 P2d 996 (1991), adhered to on reconsideration, 110 Or App 599, 823 P2d 1031 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed a circuit court judgment convicting him of supplying contraband as defined in Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.185.


OVERVIEW: The county corrections department promulgated and implemented a rule that prohibited the inmates of the county jail from possessing tobacco, matches, and rolling papers. While incarcerated at the county jail, defendant was found with all of the contraband items and charged with violating § 162.185. As used in the statute, contraband was legislatively defined as any article or thing whose use would endanger the safety and security of correctional facilities, as well as the persons in those institutions. The trial court overruled defendant's demurrer, which argued that the statute unconstitutionally delegated state legislative power to local governments. The court found that the legislature did not delegate its power to make law, but only the power to determine the existence of facts or circumstances mentioned in the law upon which the law became operative, which was constitutionally permissible. Additionally, the court found that it was constitutionally permissible for the legislature to delegate authority to local governmental bodies to adopt rules that defined or implemented broad statutory standards. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court decision that affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction by the circuit court.

 

104 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Langley


SC No. S36298


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


314 Ore. 511; 840 P.2d 691; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 209


January 23, 1991, Argued and submitted  
October 29, 1992, Decided  
October 29, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court for Marion County. Richard D. Barber, Judge. CC No. 88C21623.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of conviction for aggravated murder are reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction for aggravated murder and sentence of death in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Oregon) were submitted for automatic and direct review by the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated murder and the court took his automatic and direct appeal. The court held that the trial court erred when it admitted evidence of the murder of another person for the purpose of using some similarities between the two homicides to identify defendant as the killer of the victim in the case at bar. The court found that the record did not support a conclusion that the two murders were sufficiently similar and distinctive to warrant admission of evidence of the first murder to establish identity of the murderer of the victim based on modus operandi. The court then considered the State's contention that, if there was error in admitting evidence of the other homicide, then it was harmless error. The court held that, even though there was substantial and convincing evidence on which a reasonable jury could have found defendant guilty of the murder at issue without the evidence of the other murder, it could not be said that there was little likelihood that the error in admitting other crimes evidence affected the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated murder and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

105 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Automobile Club of Oregon v. State


SC No. S38565


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


314 Ore. 479; 840 P.2d 674; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 206


January 8, 1992, Argued and submitted  
October 29, 1992  
October 29, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding for review of Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 863, section 18, and Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 752, sections 14 to 14e.



DISPOSITION: Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 863, section 8, and Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 752, sections 14 to 14e, are invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, auto club and auto towing service, sought review of the constitutionality of respondent state's enforcement of an underground storage tank assessment and emission fee pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 319.025 and Or. Rev. Stat. § 468A.425 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The automobile club and auto towing service challenged the state's imposition of an underground storage tank assessment and emission fee, contending they were taxes in violation of Or. Const. art. IX, § 3. The automobile club and auto towing service argued that the fee and assessment were actually taxes levied against the operation or use of motor vehicles and were therefore in violation of the state constitution provision which required such taxes to be used exclusively for the construction, maintenance, or repair of public highways and roads. The court found the underground storage tank assessment was actually a tax on persons who took delivery of gasoline intended for resale into underground tanks. The court explained that an assessment was a fee imposed on property owners to finance improvements or services. The court further explained that the label attached to such a fee was not dispositive as to whether it constituted a tax. The court next found that the emission fee was a tax upon the privilege of operating a vehicle and not a graduated charge for pollution as urged by the state. The court found that the assessment and fee violated the Oregon Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the automobile club and auto towing service state constitutional challenge and invalidated the state's underground storage tank assessment and vehicle emission fee.

State v. Sullens


SC No. S38221


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


314 Ore. 436; 839 P.2d 708; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 197


November 6, 1991, Argued and submitted  
October 22, 1992  
October 22, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 89-CR-0005-TM; CA No. A62348.


*  Appeal from Deschutes County Circuit Court, Thomas M. Mosgrove, Judge. 106 Or App 590, 809 P2d 700 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed, and the case is remanded to that court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence, pursuant to Or. R. Civ. P. 64B(4), following defendant's conviction for first degree burglary and theft.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted for first degree burglary and theft, defendant filed a motion, pursuant to Or. R. Civ. P. 64B(4), for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The trial court did not rule on the motion within the statutorily specified time limit therefore the motion was deemed denied, and defendant sought review. The appellate court affirmed the denial without reaching the merits, ruling that it lacked authority to review the motion, and defendant sought further review. On appeal, the court held that the appellate court's ruling was erroneous. The court held that, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.040, orders entered after a judgment that was appealed were not reviewable, except for orders denying motions for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence or juror misconduct. The court held that based on this determination and the fact that § 138.040 had not been changed in a relevant way since the court's interpretation of the statute, the interpretation remained part of the statute. Therefore, the court reversed the decision of the appellate court and remanded defendant's motion to the appellate court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision affirming the denial of defendant's motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The court remanded the matter to the appellate court for further proceedings.

*  Appeals from Deschutes County Circuit Court (CC 90-CV-0091-TM), Thomas M. Mosgrove, Judge, 110 Or App 614, 825 P2d 657 (1992); and Marion County Circuit Court (CC 90-C-11681), Rodney W. Miller, Judge, 111 Or App 438, 825 P2d 657 (1992).



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the Court of Appeals and the judgments of the circuit courts are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review from the decision of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the trial courts' dismissal of their actions because their petitions for post-conviction relief were untimely.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were separately convicted of crimes and both filed motions for post-conviction relief. The respective post-conviction courts granted the motions to dismiss brought by respondents, state and penitentiary superintendent. The appellate court affirmed the dismissal and the court affirmed. The court found that both of the appeals centered on the applicability and the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. §138.510(2), which required petitions for post-conviction relief to be filed within 90 days of the conviction, with limited exceptions. The court determined that the statute was applicable to both defendants and was not inconsistent with §138.530(2), which concerned the substantive relief intended to be preserved by the legislature in the enactment of the statute. The court concluded that the statute did not violate the due process clause of the U.S. Constitution, did not violate Or. Const. art. I §23, or violate the U.S. Const. art. I, §9, clause 2. The court held that the statute provided a reasonable time limitation for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the appellate and trial courts.

DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court convicted defendant of intimidation in the first degree, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.165(1)(a)(A). The Oregon Court of Appeals affirmed defendant's conviction. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in overruling his demurrer. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Hendrix


SC No. S38384


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


314 Ore. 170; 838 P.2d 566; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 159


March 5, 1992, Argued and submitted  
August 27, 1992  
August 27, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. C89-12-36913; CA No. A65065.


*  Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, James R. Ellis, Judge. 107 Or App 734, 813 P2d 1115 (1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon) that affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction for the crime of intimidation in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.165(1)(a)(A).


OVERVIEW: During the assault upon which the charges were based, defendant's co-defendants were heard directing derogatory racial comments to the victims. The court affirmed the appellate court's order affirming the conviction. At the outset, the court observed that it had previously determined that § 166.165(1)(a)(A), which prohibited two or more individuals from intentionally injuring another on the basis of a perception as to the victim's race, religion, national origin, or sexual orientation, was constitutional. The court also ruled that the evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant manifested the requisite intent. The court observed that, while there was no evidence that defendant uttered any words of prejudice or hatred, he was present when his co-defendants did. Moreover, defendant observed the victims speaking little English, heard his co-defendants uttering prejudicial remarks and continued to beat the victims after the remarks were uttered, and left with the co-defendants after the assault. This evidence was sufficient for a trier of fact to reasonably infer that defendant intended to cause physical injury to the victims because of the perception of their race.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order affirming the trial court's judgment of conviction for intimidation in the first degree.

Anderson v. State

August 6, 1992

PRIOR HISTORY: On petition pursuant to Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 796, section 15, to review Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 823 (HB 2352).



DISPOSITION: On the petition to review the constitutional validity of Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 823: petitioners' claims under Article IX, section 9, of the Oregon Constitution and under various state and federal statutes are dismissed; the remainder of petitioners' claims are answered by Hughes v. State of Oregon, 314 Or 1, 838 P2d 1018 (1992).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a retired federal employee, who received a federal pension, and his wife, who had a survivorship interest in her husband's federal pension benefits, challenged the legal validity of 1991 Or. Laws ch. 823. The federal employee and his wife contended that the law violated the Contract Clauses of the state and federal constitutions, Or. Const. art. I, § 21, and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1.


OVERVIEW: The retired federal employee and his wife also contended that 1991 Or. Laws ch. 823 violated the Just Compensation Clauses of the state and federal constitutions, Or. Const. art. I, § 18, and the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. The court held that those arguments had been answered in a previous decision. In responding to the contentions of the retired federal employee and his wife that they were required to pay income tax on their federal social security benefits, for the first time, the court held that its jurisdiction in the case was limited under 1991 Or. Laws ch. 796, § 15(1) to considering whether the taxation of retirement benefits received by retired members of the Public Employes' Retirement System (PERS) and other retirement systems established by the state or political subdivisions of the state was in violation of any constitutional provision. The retired federal employee and his wife were not retired members of the PERS or other retirement systems established by the state. They did not have an interest in any retirement system of the state or of any of the political subdivisions of the state.


OUTCOME: The court held that most of the questions of the retired federal employee and his wife were answered in another decision. The court was limited to considering whether the taxation of retirement benefits received by retired members of the Public Employes' Retirement System and other retirement systems established by the state or political subdivisions of the state was in violation of any state constitutional provision.

 

112 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Hughes v. State


SC Nos. S38544 (Control), S38549, S38700, S38701 (Cases Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


314 Ore. 1; 838 P.2d 1018; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 151; 15 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2473


January 8, 1992, Argued and submitted  
August 6, 1992, Decided  
August 6, 1992, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 823, section 1, is declared unconstitutional under Article I, section 21, of the Oregon Constitution insofar as it affects retirement benefits accrued or accruing for work performed on or before September 28, 1991. The constitutional validity of Oregon Laws 1991, chapter 823, section 3, is sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, present and retired public employees, sought declaration of constitutionality of respondent state's subjecting the public employees' retirement benefits to state income taxation under 1991 Or. Laws ch. 823, §§ 1 and 3.


OVERVIEW: The present and retired public employees sought declaration of the constitutionality of the state's subjecting previously exempt public employees' retirement benefits to income tax under 1991 Or. Laws ch. 823, §§ 1 and 3. The court found 1991 Or. Laws, ch. 823, § 1 was unconstitutional to the extent it affected retirement benefits accrued or accruing for work performed on or before its effective date, explaining the statute impaired a contractual obligation in violation of the state contracts clause, Or. Const. art. I, § 21. The court explained the language contained in former Or. Rev. Stat. § 237.201 (1989) was promissory and in the context of its enactment revealed an intent to create a contract exempting public employees' retirement benefits from state and local taxation when such benefits were accrued prior to the amendment effective date. The court sustained the constitutionality of 1991 Or. Laws ch. 823, § 3 because it did not violate the contracts clause when it breached, rather than impaired public employees' contract insofar as it subjected accrued benefits to taxation. The court noted breach of contract differs from impairment of contractual obligation.


OUTCOME: Court declared the state statute subjecting the public employees' previously accrued retirement benefits to income tax unconstitutional because it violated state contracts clause by impairing a contractual obligation exempting such benefits from tax. The court sustained state's related statute that subjected accrued benefits to taxation because it breached rather than impaired a contractual obligation and was constitutional.

State v. Rogers


SC No. S36344


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


313 Ore. 356; 836 P.2d 1308; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 134


November 4, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 9, 1992  
July 9, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On automatic and direct review of the judgments of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court for Clackamas County. Raymond R. Bagley, Judge. CC Nos. 88-355, 88-356, 88-357, 88-358, 88-359, 88-360.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of conviction for aggravated murder and aggravated felony murder are affirmed. The sentence of death is vacated. The case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Clackamas County (Oregon), which entered judgments of conviction on 13 counts of aggravated murder and imposed the death penalty under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150(1)(f).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of all 13 counts of aggravated murder and found that he was eligible for the death penalty, requiring the imposition of the death penalty. Defendant sought review. The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing. The court found that: (1) defendant failed to establish the value of a public opinion poll, that there was a significant risk of error in light of extensive voir dire provided, or that the pretrial publicity precluded a fair trial; (2) the other crimes evidence was admissible to prove that defendant had the same separate objective intentionally to cause intense pain to the victims by inflicting stabbing and cutting wounds to them before killing them and the jury could reasonably infer from that evidence that defendant possessed the identical intent; (3) the issue of dangerousness was not precluded by the previous jury's determination that defendant was not dangerous at that time; (4) the sentencing jury was not asked whether the death penalty was appropriate, considering all aspects of defendant's life and crimes; and (5) the trial court properly refused an instruction as to residual doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction on all counts of aggravated murder, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing so that the sentencing jury would be given an effective opportunity to consider all aspects of defendant's life and crimes in fixing the appropriate sentence.

State v. Isom


SC No. S36612


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


313 Ore. 391; 837 P.2d 491; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 136


July 9, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 9, 1992  
July 9, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On reinstated appeal of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death entered by the Circuit Court for Multnomah County. * Stephen L. Gallagher, Judge. CC No. C86-05-32246.


* Reinstated appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Stephen L. Gallagher, Judge. 306 Or 587, 761 P2d 524 (1988).



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction for aggravated murder and sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence in the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon) for aggravated murder under Or. Rev. Stat. 163.095(2)(f).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated murder under § 163.095(2)(f) and sentenced to death for the stabbing of the victim committed after he failed to return to a work release center. On appeal, the conviction was reversed. Defendant was convicted of aggravated murder after a second trial and sentenced to death, and defendant appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. Section 163.095(2)(f) was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant because, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.035(4), the court had to sentence him under the statutory scheme in force when the criminal act was committed. Or. Rev. Section 163.095(2)(f) was applicable to defendant, although he escaped from a correctional facility in another state, because the language was clear and which state the correctional facility was located was not a crucial element of § 163.095(2)(f). Section 163.095(2)(f) was not unconstitutionally vague because it was sufficiently explicit to inform those who were subject to it of what conduct on their part would render them liable to its penalties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated murder and the death sentence.

Smith v. Clackamas County


SC No. S37571


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


313 Ore. 519; 836 P.2d 716; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 141


March 5, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 9, 1992  
July 9, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * LUBA No. 89-156; CA No. A65307.


*  Judicial review from a Final Opinion and Order of the Land Use Board of Appeals of the State of Oregon. 103 Or App 370, 797 P2d 1058 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The order of the Land Use Board of Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner on review, a landowner, sought review of a decision of a court of appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the final order of the Land Use Board of Appeals (LUBA) of the State of Oregon that affirmed the decision of respondent on review, a county, to deny the landowner's request to establish a nonfarm dwelling on seven acres zoned Exclusive Farm Use (EFU).


OVERVIEW: The county had denied the landowner's request to build a nonfarm dwelling on seven acres of his 54-acre parcel because it determined that Clackamas County, Or., Zoning and Development Ordinance 402.05.A.4 permitted such a dwelling on land zoned EFU only if it was situated upon generally unsuitable land for farm production. The county had applied the criterion to the whole 54 acres and found that 47 acres was suitable for growing trees. The landowner contended that the criterion should have been applied only to the seven acres, which were unsuitable for farming. The court agreed with the court of appeals and the LUBA that the county properly applied the criterion to the whole parcel because the appropriate course was to construe the ordinance consistently with the state policy found in Or. Rev. Stat. § 215.243. The court rejected the landowner's contention that the decisions of the court of appeals and LUBA were based on a misinterpretation of the applicable law. The court reviewed the legislative history of the statute and determined that the state land use policy was to preserve large blocks of agricultural land although that substantially limited alternative uses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals and the order of LUBA.

State v. Davis


SC No. S36889


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


313 Ore. 246; 834 P.2d 1008; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 106


September 6, 1990, Argued and submitted  
June 5, 1992  
June 5, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. A8801-30035; CA No. A50571.


*  Appeal from Order of Multnomah County Circuit Court, William C. Snouffer, Judge. 99 Or App 358, 781 P2d 1264 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part on different grounds. The order of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the reversal by the Court of Appeals (Oregon), of the trial court's grant of his pretrial motion to suppress certain statements, including a confession to a murder, made by defendant to police officers at the time of defendant's arrest while in custody out of state. Defendant argued that the admission of the confession and statements violated his constitutional rights because they were the product of an illegal arrest.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was visiting his mother's house in Mississippi, he was arrested under an Oregon fugitive warrant for failing to appear on robbery charges. The police entered the house without a search warrant. During conversation with police, defendant confessed to a murder in Oregon that was unrelated to the robbery charges. The trial court granted defendant's pretrial motions to suppress the confession and other statements about the murder. The state appealed. The appellate court reversed, but assumed, without deciding, that the entry into the house was unlawful. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed in part on different grounds. The court held that the appellate court erred in its assumption. The entry into the house was legal under Or. Const. art. I, § 9 because it was made with probable cause to believe that defendant was there. Defendant's Miranda waivers were voluntary. The fact that defendant was being interrogated for a crime for which he was not represented by counsel did not violate his Fifth or Sixth Amendment rights, his rights under Or. Const. art. I, § 11, or his rights against compelled self-incrimination under Or. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part on other grounds the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's grant of defendant's motion to suppress a confession and other statements related to a murder charge.

Elvin v. Or. Pub. Employees Union


SC No. S37333


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


313 Ore. 165; 832 P.2d 36; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 42; 140 L.R.R.M. 2347


December 4, 1990, Argued and submitted  
May 1, 1992  
May 1, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * ERB UP No. 38-87; CA No. A50465.


*  Judicial review from the Employment Relations Board. 102 Or App 159, 793 P2d 338 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the order of the Employment Relations Board are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Oregon Public Employees Union (OPEU) sought review from the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the decision of the Oregon Employment Relations Board (ERB) that found the OPEU committed unfair labor practices under the Public Employees Collective Bargaining Act (PECBA) Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.650 to § 243.782, in the way in which OPEU collected "fair share" payments from respondents' nonunion public employees.


OVERVIEW: The nonunion public employees were forced to participate in fair share payments by the OPEU in a collective bargaining unit. The nonunion public employees filed objection to the payments with the OPEU, and the parties went into arbitration. The nonunion public employees disagreed with the result and filed a case with the ERB that found the OPEU had violated the PECBA and ordered refund payments. The OPEU appealed, and the appellate court affirmed. The OPEU again sought review, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that based on the facts of the record, and the ERB's rationale for its order, the court held that the ERB permissibly imposed an order of restitution and not a civil penalty on the OPEU pursuant to the PECBA. The court found that under Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.676(2)(c) ERB had the authority to order restitution as a remedy for an unfair labor practice under PECBA because ERB believed that restitution of the fair share payments as the remedy for OPEU's violation of respondents' constitutional rights was the only practical way to vindicate those rights and that the remedy was within ERB's statutory discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court and the order of the ERB. The court found that under the PECBA, the ERB had the authority to order restitution as a remedy for unfair labor practices.

Anderson v. Department of Revenue


SC No. S38099


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


313 Ore. 1; 828 P.2d 1001; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 24


January 10, 1992, Argued and submitted  
March 26, 1992  
March 26, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 26, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. Carl N. Byers, Judge. OTC No. 3048.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Tax Court is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The decision of the Department of Revenue is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and this case is remanded to the Department with instructions to provide a refund of the excess tax paid by taxpayers for tax year 1988, and a refund of any excess tax paid by taxpayers for any tax years thereafter in which federal retirement income was included in their state taxable income at a time when, for the same tax year, state retirement income was completely exempt from state taxation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision by the Oregon Tax Court, which dismissed the taxpayers' complaint against respondent department of revenue (department) for tax refunds for the years 1975 through 1989 and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers contended that income taxes assessed by the department on the their federal retirement income were unconstitutional and that they were entitled to a refund of state income taxes. The court reversed in part the judgment of the tax court because the taxpayers were entitled to refunds of any excess tax that they paid for tax year 1988 and any tax years thereafter in which their federal retirement income was included in their state taxable income at a time when, for the same tax year, state retirement income was completely exempted from state taxation. The taxpayers' claims for money had and received, restitution in quasi-contract, setoff, recoupment, and constructive trust merely sought a refund of taxes paid under an unconstitutional scheme, for which the remedies provided in the tax refund statutes were constitutionally sufficient and exclusive. Even if the taxpayers' state constitutional claims otherwise would have been within the Oregon Tort Claims Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.320, the state explicitly had retained its immunity to the claims. The taxpayers' claims for damages based only on state constitutional violations did not state a cognizable claim for relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the tax court. The court remanded the case to the department to provide a refund of the excess tax paid by the taxpayers for tax year 1988, and a refund of any excess tax paid by the taxpayers for any tax years thereafter in which federal retirement income was included in their state taxable income.

State v. Wolfs


SC S37847


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 646; 826 P.2d 623; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 13


May 7, 1991, Argued and submitted  
February 13, 1992  
February 13, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 10-88-01844; CA No. A60331.


*  Appeal from Lane County Circuit Court, F. Gordon Cottrell, Judge. 105 Or App 5, 803 P2d 1192 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for further consideration.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Lane County Circuit Court (Oregon), which held that granting defendant's motion for "judgment of acquittal" during trial, on the sole ground that the indictment did not state facts sufficient to establish a crime, barred a later prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted as an ex-convict in possession of a concealable firearm. After the state presented its case-in-chief at trial, defendant moved for a "judgment of acquittal." He claimed that the indictment was defective in that it did not allege that the firearm was concealable. The trial court granted the motion. The state obtained a new indictment. At his second trial, defendant moved for a dismissal. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. The court of appeals reversed, holding that the second prosecution was barred by Oregon's constitutional ban against double jeopardy. The State appealed, and the court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals. The court found that defendant's motion for "judgment of acquittal" during trial, on the sole ground that the indictment did not state facts sufficient to establish a crime, did not bar a later prosecution. When defendant moved to terminate a proceeding on the sole ground that the accusatory instrument was defective, the applicable statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.505(6), and Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.445, did not bar a later prosecution. Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.525(1)(a), (b)(B).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further consideration.
