Ragsdale v. Department of Revenue


SC S37704


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 529; 823 P.2d 971; 1992 Ore. LEXIS 4; 14 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2169


July 10, 1991, Argued and submitted  
January 3, 1992  
January 3, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. * Carl N. Byers, Judge. OTC No. 2958.


*  11 OTR 440 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Oregon Tax Court is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The decision of the Department of Revenue is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and this case is remanded to the Department with instructions to provide a refund of $ 2,518, the excess tax paid by the taxpayer for tax year 1988, and a refund of any excess tax paid by the taxpayer for any tax years thereafter in which federal retirement income was included in her state taxable income at a time when, for the same tax year, state retirement income was completely exempt from state taxation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Oregon Tax Court, which upheld appellee Department of Revenue's denial of her claim for tax refunds for taxes paid. The taxpayer claimed that pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 305.765 to § 305.785, she was entitled to a refund of state income tax paid on her federal retirement income because the intergovernmental tax immunity rendered the tax on her federal retirement income invalid.


OVERVIEW: The tax court upheld the department's denial of the taxpayer's claim for a refund for taxes paid on her federal retirement income. On appeal, the court reversed in part, ruling that because federal retirement benefits were subject to a limited exemption from state tax while state benefits were completely exempt, Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.680(1)(c) and (d) impermissibly discriminated against federal employees in violation of the constitutional doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity. Thus, the court ruled, under § 305.765, the taxpayer was entitled to file an action for a refund for the excess taxes she paid due to the inclusion of federal pension and retirement income in her state taxable income. The court held, however, that she was not entitled to a refund for prior years because, under § 305.765 and § 305.780, an action for refunds of taxes collected in years prior to the year in which the action resulting in invalidation was instituted was barred. The court concluded that the taxpayer was entitled to a refund for the taxes she paid in the year in which she filed her action, and any year thereafter, due to the inclusion of federal retirement income in her state taxable income.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's judgment in part, and reversed in part. The court remanded the case to the department with instructions to provide a refund for the excess tax paid by the taxpayer for tax year in which she filed her action for a refund, and a refund of any excess tax paid by the taxpayer for any tax years thereafter in which federal retirement income was improperly included in her state taxable income.

Laws 932, § 2 did not violate the Separation of Powers Clause of Or. Const. art. III, § 1.

Moen v. Peterson


SC S37764


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 503; 824 P.2d 404; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 99


April 3, 1991, Argued and submitted  
December 19, 1991  
December 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 87C-11030; CA No. A61667.


*  Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Val D. Sloper, Judge. 104 Or App 481, 802 P2d 76 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed on different grounds. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest to charges of sodomy in the first degree in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.405. Defendant received a 10-year minimum sentence pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 144.110(1). A court of appeals (Oregon) affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's post-conviction request to set aside his plea for alleged inadequate assistance of counsel. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that defendant's trial counsel did not inform him of the possibility of a minimum sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 144.110. Further, the court found that defendant was aware prior to entry of his no contest plea of the possibility of a minimum sentence. Because trial counsel failed to provide the sentencing information, the court held that defendant received inadequate assistance of trial counsel. The court modified its holding in a prior case to require, in a post-conviction proceeding, that a defendant who was not advised, and did not know, of an applicable minimum sentence, also had to prove by a preponderance of the evidence facts that demonstrated prejudice. The court remanded the case to the post-conviction court for further proceedings on the issue of prejudice and thus affirmed the decision of the appellate court, which also remanded the case, on different grounds. The court found that the appellate court's grounds were in error because the holding in the prior case was not a new rule to be applied retroactively, but the reapplication of an old rule announced in an earlier case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case to the post-conviction court for further proceedings so that defendant could present more evidence on the issue of prejudice. The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court on different grounds.

Baker v. Keisling


SC S38512 (Cases Consolidated for Opinion) SC S38511


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 385; 822 P.2d 1162; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 83


October 7, 1991, Baker and Allen petition submitted; October 8, 1991, Gernant and Remington petition was argued and submitted  
December 12, 1991  
December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petitions to review ballot title.



DISPOSITION: Ballot title certified as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens challenged a certified ballot title for an initiative measure amending the Oregon Constitution in a suit involving respondents.


OVERVIEW: The citizens brought two separate petitions challenging a certified ballot title for an initiative measure amending the Oregon Constitution. Each petition raised the issue whether the caption, question, and summary were sufficient to perform the office assigned to them by statute. The court held that the use of only the verb "promote" in the caption failed to identify the subject of the measure, because the measure went beyond proscribing promotion to proscribe any facilitation by any level of government, and because the measure required all levels of government to assist in setting a standard for youth that discourages the types of sexual activity named in the measure. The certified caption was so narrowly phrased as to cause the voter, for whose use the caption was intended, to be inaccurately informed about the scope and coverage of the measure. The court held that the summary did not disclose some major effects of the measure. The certified summary made no reference to the requirement that the listed behaviors "were to be discouraged." Accordingly, the summary was altered to include a reference to that major effect of the measure.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the ballot title certified as modified in a suit involving the citizens and respondents.

 

127 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Davey v. Frankel


SC S36568


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 286; 823 P.2d 394; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 89


June 7, 1990, Argued and submitted  
December 12, 1991  
December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding in mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ to issue requiring vacation of order of circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The relator, a defendant in a criminal proceeding in the Multnomah Circuit Court (Oregon), sought a peremptory writ of mandamus requiring the trial court judge to vacate the order excluding the public from a hearing under Or. Evid. Code 412, also known as the "Rape Shield Law."


OVERVIEW: The relator was charged with third degree rape and sodomy. There was no dispute that the relator had complied with the statutory prerequisites entitling him to a pretrial hearing under Or. Evid. Code 412 to determine the admissibility of evidence of the victim's past sexual behavior. The trial court, however, issued an order excluding the public from the Or. Evid. Code 412 hearing. The court had earlier issued an alternative writ of mandamus, requiring that the trial court judge vacate the order or show cause why it should not. The court held that a peremptory writ of mandamus was proper because if the relator was correct that the Or. Evid. Code 412 hearing was open to the public, the fact that a closed hearing was held was a separate harm that could not be undone. After construing the statute, the court found that the trial court acted under an erroneous perception of its legal duty. The court held that "in chambers," as used in Or. Evid. Code 412(3)(b), meant that the hearing must take place in the judge's office, commonly referred to as the judge's "chambers." The court held that the statute did not categorically exclude the public from attending.


OUTCOME: A peremptory writ was issued requiring the trial court to vacate its order.

Ater v. Keisling


Nos. S38475, S38476, S38477, S38478, S38479 consolidated


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 207; 819 P.2d 296; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 77


October 2, 1991, Argued and submitted  
October 15, 1991  
October 15, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petitions for review of the reapportionment plan submitted by the Secretary of State pursuant to Oregon Constitution, Article IV, section 6(3).



DISPOSITION: The Ater (S38475), Bugas (S38477), and Caballero (S38479) petitions are dismissed. The Paulk (S38478) and Linder (S38476) petitions are granted. The reapportionment plan is voided and returned to the Secretary of State with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, five separate groups of citizens, sought review of the reapportionment plan that had been submitted by the respondent Secretary of State (secretary).


OVERVIEW: Five separate groups of citizens sought review of the reapportionment of their districts and argued that the secretary's plan failed to comply with Or. Const. art. IV, § 6(1). The court dismissed three of the petitions. Or. Rev. Stat. 188.010(1) required that the secretary "consider" the five criteria: that each district, as nearly as practicable, shall be: contiguous, of equal population, utilize existing geographic or political boundaries, not divide communities of common interest; and be connected by transportation links. Where the statutory goals collided, the reapportionment process necessarily required some flexibility in application. The record was replete with evidence that the secretary did consider all five statutory criteria and the choices made in drawing the district boundaries at issue in three of the petitions were consistent with Or. Const. art. IV, § 6(1) and Or. Rev. Stat. 188.010. Because of mistakes made by the secretary in dividing the districts in the two remaining petitions, the court voided the reapportionment and the secretary was directed to correct the errors in one of the petitions and to reconsider the district assignments in the other.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed three of the petitions and granted two of the petitions filed by the five separate groups of citizens seeking review of the reapportionment plant submitted by the secretary. The reapportionment plan was voided and returned to the secretary with instructions.

State v. Galligan


SC No. S37809


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 35; 816 P.2d 601; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 60


May 7, 1991, Argued and submitted  
August 29, 1991  
August 29, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * DC DA No. 415 327A; CA No. A65406.


* Appeal from Multnomah County District Court, Michael Marcus, Judge pro tempore, 105 Or App 131, 803 P2d 787 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the affirmance by the Court of Appeals (Oregon) of his conviction for the crime of unauthorized departure under Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.175.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the crime of unauthorized departure under § 162.175 when, as an inmate at a corrections facility, he was given authorization to leave the facility for a work-release program but failed to return to the facility at the appointed time. Defendant appealed on the ground that Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.135(3) stated that "custody" did not include detention in a correctional facility. The court of appeals affirmed the conviction. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed, holding that the word "custody," as used in Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.135(7), included detention in a correctional facility. The court determined that the legislature clearly intended that the crime of unauthorized departure be directed at those inmates who failed to return after temporary leave from a correctional facility. The legislative history demonstrated that to assign the Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.135(3) definition of "custody" to the word "custody," as used in Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.135(7), would have voided the entire last clause of § 162.135(7) and entirely thwarted the legislative intent. In amending § 162.135(7), the legislature merely overlooked the need to amend Or. Rev. Stat. 162.135(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals affirming defendant's conviction for the crime of unauthorized departure.

Mathias v. Department of Revenue


SC No. S37159


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


312 Ore. 50; 817 P.2d 272; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 62


September 5, 1990, Argued and submitted  
August 29, 1991  
August 29, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. * Carl N. Byers, Judge. OTC No. 2910.


* 11 OTR 347 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Oregon Tax Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of revenue challenged the judgment of the Oregon Tax Court, which held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 308.205, requiring taxpayers who owned at least four parcels of land to be taxed at a higher rate than taxpayers who owed three or fewer, violated Or. Const. art. I, § 32's prohibition against imposing a non-uniform tax.


OVERVIEW: The state department of revenue imposed a higher value upon respondent taxpayer's four lots in a subdivision than upon identical lots adjacent to it in the same subdivision under the authority of Or. Rev. Stat. § 308.205, thereby requiring him to pay a higher ad valorem tax. The taxpayer objected, claiming that under Or. Const. art. I, § 32, all taxation shall be uniform on the same class of subjects within the territorial limits of the authority levying the tax. The tax court found in the taxpayer's favor, finding that § 308.205 was illegal and discriminatory. The state department of revenue appealed the ruling, and the court held that there was no rational difference between the taxpayer's lots and identical lots adjacent to it. The court determined that § 308.205 was discriminatory and not uniform, because there was no justification for assessing a higher value of the taxpayer's property over identical lots nearby. The court affirmed the lower court, and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed. These cases are remanded to the tax court with instruction to vacate the "judgment," leaving in place the intermediate order that reflects the partial disposition of defendants' motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporations appealed from the decision of the Oregon Tax Court, which enforced plaintiff Department of Revenue's subpoena against them.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Revenue (Department) requested information concerning the purchase price of potato processing plants which the corporations had acquired. R. Civ. P. 67 B did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the corporations' appeal.

Seto v. Tri-County Metro. Transp. Dist.


SC No. S38056


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


311 Ore. 456; 814 P.2d 1060; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 40


June 11, 1991, Argued and submitted  
July 5, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On judicial review from the Land Use Board of Appeals. * LUBA No. 91-045.


*  Appeal from the Final Order of the Tri-County Metropolitan Transportation District of Oregon.



DISPOSITION: The Final Opinion and Recommendation of the Land Use Board of Appeals is affirmed. The Final Order of the Tri-County Metropolitan Transportation District of Oregon is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, local citizens affected by the proposed location of a light rail route, sought review of the final opinion and recommendation of the Land Use Board of Appeals (Oregon), which recommended that the final order of respondent, the Tri-County Metropolitan Transportation District of Oregon (Tri-Met), be affirmed.


OVERVIEW: The citizens claimed that S.B. 573, 1991 Or. Laws 3 (Act), was unconstitutional because, inter alia, it deprived the affected local governments of their home rule rights under the federal and state constitutions. They also claimed that Tri-Met exceed its statutory authority because it did not hold a public hearing on the environmental impact statement. The court affirmed the appeals board's decision and Tri-Met's final order. The court found no error requiring remand because: 1) Tri-Met acted in accordance with its statutory authority under the alternative land use siting process established by the Act; 2) the Act did not offend constitutional home rule provisions because it was a general law addressed to legitimate state objectives, and it not interfere with the local governments' choice of government; 3) the citizens demonstrated no violation of their constitutional rights based on the Act's standing requirements; 4) the Act did not require Tri-Met to hold a public hearing on the impact statement; and 5) Tri-Met complied with the criteria established for it to use in making decisions on the light rail route related to adverse impacts and adequate mitigation measures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the final opinion and recommendation of the appeals board and the Tri-Met final order.

 

136 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Nutbrown v. Munn


SC S36652


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


311 Ore. 328; 811 P.2d 131; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 31


May 2, 1990, Argued and submitted  
May 9, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oregon Tax Court. Carl N. Byers, Judge. TC No. 2867.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Oregon Tax Court dismissing Taxpayers' complaint is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a decision of the Oregon Tax Court, which dismissed the taxpayers' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 complaint against defendants, the Department of Revenue (department) and state officials, for their taxation of federal retirement benefits. The tax court dismissed the complaint pursuant to Or. Tax Ct. R. 21 based upon the taxpayers' failure to exhaust administrative remedies, as required by Or. Rev. Stat. § 305.275(4).


OVERVIEW: Oregon, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.680(1)(c), imposed an income tax on federal retirement benefits received by the taxpayers, but exempted retirement benefits of former state employees. The taxpayers asserted in their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim that the disparate treatment was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the tax court's judgment dismissing the taxpayers' action. The court held that a state might impose an exhaustion requirement without offending federal law because the general rule that civil rights actions could be brought in state court without exhausting state administrative remedies did not apply to actions relating to the state's method of assessing and collecting taxes. Because exhaustion was consistent with the Tax Injunction Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1341, the court found that Or. Rev. Stat. § 305.275(4) was constitutionally valid. The court further held that the scope of the exhaustion requirement of § 305.274(4) applied to declaratory and injunctive relief, as well as to a claim for damages. The court found that the taxpayers were not excused from the requirement on the ground that the department lacked authority to grant them all of the relief sought.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's judgment dismissing the taxpayers' § 1983 action against the department and state officials.

State v. Benton


SC No. S37184


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


311 Ore. 295; 810 P.2d 851; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 30


January 22, 1991, Argued and submitted  
May 2, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * DC No. B63-787; CA No. A61763.


*  Appeal from Lane County District Court, Winfrid K. Liepe, Judge. 101 Or App 386, 790 P2d 1191, 102 Or App 585, 795 P2d 601 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The sentence is vacated and the case is remanded to the district court for resentencing for civil contempt; otherwise, the judgment of the district court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the State of Oregon, appealed the order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversing the judgment of a trial court holding petitioner in contempt of court for his wilful failure to pay restitution in connection with a conviction on bad check charges and ordering him to serve three days in jail. The appeals court had ruled that Ore. Rev. Stat. § 161.685 did not authorize imposition of a determinate sentence for civil contempt.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to pay restitution in connection with his conviction for negotiating bad checks. When he failed to do so, he was ordered to show cause why he should not be held in contempt as a result thereof. His motion to dismiss the show cause order was denied, and he was tried, convicted, and sentenced to three days in jail pursuant to § 161.685. On appeal, the appeals court reversed, agreeing with petitioner that a determinate sentence could only be imposed where the contempt proceeding was criminal, not civil. On the State's appeal, the court affirmed. It held that a penalty was "civil" when it was imposed to compel compliance with an order and ended as soon as compliance was had. Because it had imposed a determinate sentence, the court ruled that the district court had erred. It affirmed the appellate court decision, vacated the sentence, and remanded the case to the district court for resentencing for civil contempt. Otherwise, however, the district court judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court judgment, vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing, and affirmed the balance of the district court order.

Coalition for Equitable School Funding, Inc. v. State


SC No. S37429


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


311 Ore. 300; 811 P.2d 116; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 27


November 7, 1990, Argued and submitted  
May 2, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Richard D. Barber, Judge. CC No. 89C-12361; CA No. A65419.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed on different grounds.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, 55 Oregon school districts, taxpayers, parents, and others, appealed the judgment of the circuit court (Oregon) that dismissed plaintiffs' action alleging that the Legislative Assembly had failed to provide by law for the establishment of a uniform and general system of common schools, in violation of Or. Const. art. VIII, § 3, in its class action against defendants, state and state board of education (the state).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs presented constitutional challenges relying on the concepts that the state should have centrally funded whatever it required of the schools and that the constitution did not countenance disparities from one school district to another, with respect to either financial benefits or tax burdens. The court ruled that Measure 5, Or. Const. art XI, §§ 11b-11f, did not render the case moot. On the merits of the case, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment on different grounds, holding that plaintiffs had failed to plead a valid claim because it found that Oregon's method of funding public schools did not violate the Oregon Constitution. The court concluded that Or. Const. art. VIII, § 3 (Safety Net), specifically addressed the funding of public schools, requiring reliance on local property taxes as a source of public school funding, including funding needed to meet state standards. It contemplated and permitted district-to-district differences in what taxpayers paid and what school children received in per-pupil spending. The court limited its decision to the constitutionality of the system of financing and not whether it was politically or educationally desirable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment on different grounds in favor of the state in plaintiffs' class action alleging that the Legislative Assembly had failed to provide by law for the establishment of a uniform and general system of common schools.

State v. Stevens


SC No. S35888


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


311 Ore. 119; 806 P.2d 92; 1991 Ore. LEXIS 16


September 5, 1990, Argued and submitted  
February 7, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Remand from the Oregon Supreme Court August 18, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ore. LEXIS 84.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court for Linn County; on certification from the Court of Appeals of noncapital convictions and sentences. William O. Lewis, Judge. CC No. CM88020368.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; sentence of death vacated; case remanded to the circuit court with instructions to delete reference to dangerous offender statute in relation to sentences on counts VIII, XI, and XII (assault in the second degree, sexual abuse in the first degree) and to conduct further proceedings on counts I, II, and III (aggravated murder) consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of aggravated murder and sentenced to death. Such convictions and sentence were subject to automatic and direct review. Defendant also was convicted of, and sentenced for, several noncapital felonies. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) certified the noncapital convictions and sentences for review.


OVERVIEW: A mother permitted defendant to drive her three oldest daughters home, but defendant took the girls to his residence and sexually assaulted them. After the daughters were reported missing, the police located defendant's residence. Noting that defendant's car contained children's items, the police entered the house and found two naked girls in the bedroom. A subsequent search revealed the missing girl's strangled corpse. After he was apprehended, defendant consented to a third search of the home and made a full confession. As charged, defendant was convicted three counts of aggravated murder, four counts of first-degree kidnapping, two counts of first-degree sexual abuse, one count of first-degree rape, and two counts of second-degree assault. Defendant appealed. On review, the court held that exigent circumstances and consent justified the warrantless searches. Moreover, by a preponderance of the evidence, defendant's consent to the third search and his confessions were given voluntarily. However, defendant was entitled to resentencing on the murder convictions because the trial court's instructions unconstitutionally limited how the jury could consider mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but vacated the death sentence and remanded for resentencing.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendants, husband and wife, of manufacture and possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Acting on a tip that there was marijuana growing on defendants' property, two deputy sheriffs chartered a helicopter to fly over the property. The lower appellate court held that the evidence obtained must be suppressed. The state sought review. Reversing the lower appellate court, the court held that the deputies did not impermissibly intrude on defendants' privacy interest, therefore, their actions did not constitute a search within the constitutional meaning.

State v. Clowes


SC No. S36922, SC No. S36946, SC No. S36933, SC No. S36946, (Cases Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 686; 801 P.2d 789; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 367


June 6, 1990, Argued and submitted  
November 26, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * DA Nos. 372447-8806, 372448-8806, 372450-8806, 372446-8806; CA Nos. A50128 (Control), A50129, A50132, A50136.


*  Appeal from Multnomah County District Court, William J. Keys, Judge. 100 Or App 266, 785 P2d 1071 (1990).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the Multnomah County District Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Oregon) affirmed defendants' convictions of criminal trespass. Defendants were charged with the offense after they attempted to prevent women from having abortions at an abortion clinic. Defendants appealed their convictions and the order that granted the state's motion to exclude evidence of their choice of evils defense, which they tendered pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.200.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that their violation of the criminal trespass law was an emergency measure that was necessary to avoid the imminent death of unborn children. They contended that the trial court erred as a matter of law in excluding evidence in support of their choice of evils defense, Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.200, which precluded them from arguing their only putative defense to the criminal trespass charge to the jury. The court affirmed the convictions and held that defendants were not entitled to assert the choice of evils defense. The court observed that the choice of evils defense was not available if it was "inconsistent with some other provision of law," as stated in Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.200(1). The court found that the defense was not available because the actions that defendants sought to prevent were actions permitted under Oregon law and the interests that defendants sought to vindicate were not consistent with the legislative decision to permit abortions. The court also stated that the defense was not available because abortion was not a "public or private injury," as that language had meaning in the context of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.200(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions of criminal trespass following their attempts to prevent or dissuade women from having abortions at an abortion clinic.

In re Complaint of Fadeley


SC No. S37022


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 548; 802 P.2d 31; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 353


June 7, 1990, Argued and submitted  
November 19, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of the Findings of Fact, Conclusions of Law and Recommendation of the Commission on Judicial Fitness and Disability of the State of Oregon. No. 89-13.



DISPOSITION: The Accused is censured.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commission on Judicial Fitness and Disability of the State of Oregon filed a complaint against accused judge for misconduct after he personally solicited campaign funds. The Commission found that the judge's actions violated the Or. Code. of Jud. Conduct, Canons 7B(7) and 7D and recommended censure.


OVERVIEW: The judge personally solicited campaign funds during his candidacy for judicial office. The Commission concluded that the judge's conduct violated Canons 7B(7) and 7D and recommended censure. The court heard the matter on mandatory review under Or. Rev. Stat. § 1.430(1). The court agreed with the Commission's findings and recommendation, holding that the Commission had jurisdiction to discipline the judge for his actions and that neither Or. Const. art. VII, § 8(e) nor Or. Rev. Stat. § 1.420 limited the power of the Commission or the court to inquire into the judge's wrongful conduct. The court found that Or. Code of Jud. Conduct, Canon 7B(7) did not offend the judge's free speech rights under Or. Const. art. I, § 8 or the First Amendment. The court reasoned that the degree of interference with the First Amendment rights of the judge was minimal, the state's interest in protecting the integrity of its judiciary was profound, and the means chosen to carry out the state's purpose were the least intrusive possible if there was to be any chance to achieve the desired aim. The court agreed that censure was the appropriate sanction.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the Commission that the judge committed misconduct and that censure was the appropriate sanction.

Zockert v. Fanning


SC No. S36272


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 514; 800 P.2d 773; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 349


October 4, 1989, Argued and submitted  
November 8, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 8805-63105; CA No. A49299.


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, William McLennan, Judge. 96 Or App 769, 775 P2d 346 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed, the decree of the circuit court is vacated, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought review of a judgment from the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon), which affirmed the judgment terminating the father's parental rights and granting an adoption to respondent adoptive parents.


OVERVIEW: The father of a minor child appealed the judgment that terminated his parental rights and decreed an adoption in favor of the adoptive parents. The issues raised on appeal were the applicable standard of proof for terminating a parent's status as the parent of a child subject to the adoption and whether that parent, if indigent, had a right to state-paid counsel. The court reversed and vacated, holding that there was no question that giving an indigent parent an opportunity to receive assistance of appointed counsel to protect parental rights was a privilege within the meaning of Or. Const. art. I, § 20. Further, the court held that denial of the father's request for appointed counsel, made absent any further inquiry about indigency in fact, denied him equality of the privilege of counsel which was granted, upon the same terms, to other parents. The court found that the privilege of having counsel appointed in termination cases under Or. Rev. Stat. § 419 applied equally to terminations by adoption under Or. Rev. Stat. § 109. Additionally, the court held that clear and convincing standard was required under Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.324.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the judgment that granted an adoption in favor of the adoptive parents and that terminated the father's rights to his minor child.

Kane v. Roberts


SC No. S37288


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 423; 799 P.2d 639; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 344


September 5, 1990, Argued and submitted  
October 25, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petition to review ballot title.



DISPOSITION: Ballot title certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen brought an original proceeding to challenge a ballot title for a proposed initiative measure that would amend the Oregon Constitution to provide a right to privacy.


OVERVIEW: The certified ballot title briefly summarized the measure and quoted its text. Arguing that the caption, question, and summary were incomplete and misleading, the objecting citizen proposed that the certified ballot title should include a comment that laws forbidding private use and possession of illegal drugs would be unenforceable if the measure were adopted. The court found that the certified ballot title substantially complied with the requirements of Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.035. The caption accurately identified the subject of the measure, as required by § 250.035(1)(a), and the question plainly phrased the chief purpose of the measure, as required by § 250.035(1)(b). The perceived motivation of the proponents in sponsoring a ballot measure was irrelevant to the determination of the chief purpose of the measure.The court further found that the summary, in quoting the words of the proposed amendment, complied with § 250.035(1)(c). The major effect of the measure was that it would amend the state constitution to add specific language establishing the right to privacy. Speculation about potential secondary effects, such as legalization of drugs, would be inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the certified ballot title substantially complied with statutory requirements.

State v. Simonsen


SC No. S36085


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 412; 798 P.2d 241; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 335


June 6, 1990, Argued and submitted  
October 4, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court in Coos County. Richard L. Barron, Judge. TC No. 88CR1816.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's convictions on two counts of aggravated murder are affirmed. Defendant's sentence of death is vacated, and the case is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court, Coos County (Oregon), the court considered the penalty phase of the trial proceedings against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of aggravated murder. His jury affirmatively answered the penalty phase questions put to it, and the trial court sentenced defendant to death. The court found that the only issue before it concerned the penalty phase of the proceedings. The court held that the penalty phase was erroneously conducted. It therefore vacated defendant's death sentence and remanded the case. Defendant argued that his penalty phase hearing was flawed because the trial court failed to instruct the jury concerning what had come to be called the "fourth question" in death penalty proceedings. The question permitted a jury to spare a defendant from the death penalty even though the evidence required a "yes" answer to the three special dispositional questions set out in former Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150(1). The "fourth question" was not submitted to the jury in defendant's case. The penalty phase hearing was, therefore, constitutionally flawed. A new proceeding was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated murder, but vacated his death sentence. The court remanded the case to the trial court for a new penalty proceeding or, at the prosecution's election, entry of life sentences.

Crumpton v. Roberts


SC No. S37471


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 381; 798 P.2d 1100; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 333


September 18, 1990, Argued and submitted  
September 27, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 2, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Marion County Circuit Court; on certification from the Court of Appeals. Richard D. Barber, Judge. CC No. 90C-11372; CA No. A66349.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a registered voter and taxpayer, filed an action against defendant state officials, seeking judicial review of an order in other than a contested case under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.484 as well as a declaratory judgment under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 246.910 and 28.010. The Marion County Circuit Court (Oregon) granted the state officials summary judgment in their favor. The voter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The voter asked the trial court for a judgment declaring that the Oregon Secretary of State acted unlawfully when she verified petition signatures gathered on or after October 3, 1989 on signature sheets which did not disclose the paid status of the petition circulators. The court found that the amendment to Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.045(5) required that all initiative petition signature sheets circulated on and after October 3, 1989 had to contain a statement noting whether any petition circulator would be paid for obtaining signatures. The court held that the legislature intended stability for the elections process and that the amendment to § 250.045(5) was not designed to interfere with an ongoing process. In affirming, the court held that the legislature did not intend that, effective October 3, 1989, all signature-collecting efforts were to cease until the Secretary approved a new initiative petition form for all initiatives previously approved. Rather, the court found that it was more reasonable to expect that the legislature intended, as the statute implied, that the new requirements were to apply only to initiative petitions approved after the statute's effective date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment in the state officials' favor.

 

148 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guzek


SC No. S35051


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 299; 797 P.2d 1031; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 331


February 8, 1990, Argued and submitted  
September 20, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 28, 1990.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Guzek, 322 Or. 245, 906 P.2d 272, 1995 Ore. LEXIS 132 (1995)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by State v. Guzek, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 137 (Or., Mar. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court of Deschutes County. Thomas M. Mosgrove, Judge. TC No. 87-CR-0373-TM.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of conviction for aggravated murder affirmed. Sentences of death vacated. Case remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court on automatic and direct review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Deschutes County (Oregon), which convicted defendant of aggravated murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two co-conspirators shot the victims and burglarized their house pursuant to a plan laid out by defendant. Defendant had dated the victims' niece and resented them for breaking up the relationship. Defendant was charged in connection with the murders after he was implicated by his co-conspirators. The co-conspirators testified against him at trial in return for a plea bargain and he was convicted. He was then sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the guilty verdicts. There was ample justification for the prosecutor's decision not to offer defendant the plea agreement he offered one of the co-conspirators because defendant maintained he had nothing to do with the murders and defendant was the leader of the group. However, the court vacated his death sentence. Defendant did not receive a proper penalty phase trial because the jury instructions did not meet constitutional requirements. The jury was not given the full range of authority to consider and act on mitigating evidence that the United States Constitution required. Defendant's additional challenges on constitutional grounds were not well taken because the court had previously rejected them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction for aggravated murder. The court vacated the sentences of death and remanded the case to the trial court for a new penalty phase proceeding.

 

149 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Mid-County Future Alternatives Comm. v. City of Portland


SC No. S36060


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


310 Ore. 152; 795 P.2d 541; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 205


November 1, 1989, Argued and submitted  
July 17, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. A8711-06867; CA No. A48513.


*  Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Katherine H. O'Neil, Judge pro tempore. 95 Or App 556, 770 P2d 604 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory action, petitioners, persons who lived throughout the area subject to annexation, challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon) that affirmed the trial court and granted summary judgment for respondents, persons living in the annexed area, dismissed the petitioners' complaint, and declared that 1987 Or. Laws ch. 818, § 3 was constitutional. The law concerned the city's annexation of property by a boundary change.


OVERVIEW: The Portland Metropolitan Area Boundary Commission ordered the annexations, which followed the procedures set out in the triple-majority annexation statutory scheme, Or. Rev. Stat. § 199.495(1). The law allowed the boundary commission to approve annexation after receiving a request signed by more than half the owners in the proposed annexation territory, who owned more than half the land in the territory, and represented more than half the assessed value of the lad. The procedure prevented other landowners from objecting to the annexation and forcing a vote. The law did not violate the home rule provisions of the state constitution. The annexations in this case did not implicate city government and any home rule authority until after the annexations were complete. The charters of the concerned cities both allowed annexation and the legislature was an agency with the legal power to modify municipal boundaries. Further, a right to vote objection to the statute was not justified by any statutory or constitutional text. There was no automatic right to vote on the extension of city authority over property one owned when the legislature created the extension. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Montez

DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed as to the guilt phase and is reversed as to the penalty phase, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for resentencing consistent with this opinion. See State v. Wagner, 309 Or 5, 786 P2d 93 (1990); see also Penry v. Lynaugh, 492 U.S.   , 109 S Ct 2934, 106 L Ed 2d 256 (1989).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On automatic and direct review pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150(1)(f), defendant sought of review of his conviction of aggravated murder and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court for Multnomah County (Oregon).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated murder and sentenced to death in connection with the murder of a woman who was strangled, doused with flammable liquid, and set on fire. On appeal, the court affirmed the guilt phase of the decision, and reversed the penalty phase and remanded for resentencing. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction in the guilt phase of the trial, but reversed the penalty phase of the trial and remanded back to the trial court for resentencing.

 

152 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. Clark


Nos. TC 9002-01034, SC S36962


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 464; 790 P.2d 1; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 35


March 15, 1990, Argued and submitted  
March 21, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 18, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Harl H. Haas, Judge. TC No. 9002-01034.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenors, a citizens' group, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which granted plaintiff voters' action for a declaratory judgment seeking to have a measure regarding the renaming of a street removed from a ballot as an improper subject for an initiative measure under Or. Const. art. IV, § 1(5).


OVERVIEW: After a city council adopted a resolution for renaming streets, the council renamed a street "Martin Luther King, Jr., Boulevard." The council thereafter passed an ordinance prescribing a policy for renaming streets. A measure submitted by defendant citizen was subsequently added to a ballot with the question whether the boulevard should be renamed "Union Avenue." The voters brought the declaratory judgment action, the circuit court removed the measure from the ballot, and the citizens' group appealed. The court affirmed and held that, although the original defendants did not actively dispute the claim, the matter was made justiciable by the participation of the citizens' group as intervenors. Hence, the judicial power of the state was properly invoked to resolve the controversy. Further, as the proposed measure would rename a street, it would do something that was governed by an ordinance in place at the time that the measure was filed. Finally, the proposed measure dealt with administrative matters, not legislation, and, therefore, the proposed measure did not qualify for the ballot because it was not "municipal legislation" under the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court removing the measure regarding the renaming of a street from the ballot.

 

153 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Van Wormer v. Salem


Nos. TC 87-C-11334, CA A47630, SC S36156


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 404; 788 P.2d 443; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 25


November 2, 1989, Argued and submitted  
March 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 87-C-11334; CA No. A47630.


*  Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, C. Gregory West, Judge. 96 Or App 107, 771 P2d 653 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed and the judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representative sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which upheld the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.275(8) as applied and affirmed the order of the trial court. The trial court had granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, city and police officer, in the personal representative's wrongful death action, relying on the two-year limitation period in § 30.275(8).


OVERVIEW: Decedent was killed by a police officer acting as an on-duty uniformed officer within the scope of his employment with the city. The personal representative of the decedent's estate filed a civil action more than two years after the shooting. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment on the ground that the claim was not timely filed. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the action. The appeals court affirmed. The personal representative claimed that § 30.275(8) and § 30.020(1) unconstitutionally created two distinct classes of tort victims: those with wrongful death claims against governmental bodies, for which the limitations period was two years, and those with wrongful death claims against everyone else, for which the period was three years. The court affirmed, finding that there was nothing unconstitutional about the distinction. Those persons who suffered a governmentally-inflicted wrongful death were merely a subset of those who had suffered wrongful death at the hands of tortfeasors generally. The subset existed only as part of the statutory scheme and was not based on any characteristic, such as race, sex, or religious affiliation, of the subset's members.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appeals court, which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the city and police officer and dismissal of the personal representative's wrongful death action as untimely.

 

154 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Whipple v. Department of Revenue


Nos. OTC 2677, SC S35882


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 422; 788 P.2d 994; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 28


October 31, 1989, Argued and submitted  
March 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. * Carl N. Byers, Judge. OTC No. 2677.


* 11 OTR 117 (1988).



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Tax Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a judgment by the Oregon Tax Court, which upheld the order of the Oregon Department of Revenue disallowing the taxpayers' claimed deduction for Canadian income taxes pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.071(2). After the taxpayers paid Canadian income taxes on Canadian investments, they sought and were denied a foreign tax credit on their federal and Oregon income taxes.


OVERVIEW: For four years, the taxpayers claimed a foreign tax credit on the Canadian taxes they paid for income from their Canadian investments. For the same years, the taxpayers claimed that the Canadian taxes were deductible as a business expense on their Oregon income tax returns. The Department disallowed the deductions and assessed taxes, penalties, and interest. The tax court sustained that order, and the court affirmed the tax court's judgment. The court held that the legislature did not intend that Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.716, providing for a general deduction for foreign taxes, would repeal Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.071(2), which limited the amount of foreign tax deductions to $ 7,000. The first statute was a general statute relating to use of a credit on federal income taxes while § 316.071(2) specifically addressed the amount of taxes that could be deducted as foreign country tax and was an exception to the provisions in Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.716. Thus, only those foreign taxes as specified in Or. Rev. Stat. § 316.071 could be a basis for a claimed statutory foreign tax deduction. As the taxpayers did not qualify for the deduction under § 316.071, the tax court properly denied the credit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the tax court's judgment disallowing the taxpayers' claimed deduction for Canadian income taxes.

Sealey v. Hicks


Nos. TC 86-0869C, CA A47084, SC S36025


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 387; 788 P.2d 435; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 33; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,407


June 14, 1989, Argued and submitted  
March 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 86-0869C; CA No. A47084.


*  Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Nancy W. Campbell, Judge pro tempore. 95 Or App 182, 768 P2d 428 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff auto passenger filed a products liability action against defendant corporation, but summary judgment was granted for the corporation. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) ruled that Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905(1) was constitutional, and the passenger did not allege a failure to warn.


OVERVIEW: A passenger was seriously injured in an auto accident. He brought a products liability action against a corporation, but it was ruled that the action was time barred by § 30.905(1). The passenger argued that § 30.905(1) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the court of appeals' order. It held that Or. Const. art. I, § 10, did not apply to the passenger. The legislature had the authority to determine what constituted a legally cognizable injury, and it had not deprived the passenger of a preexisting remedy for his injury. The passenger was not deprived of any right or privilege because of his age. The classifications made by Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905(1) had a rational relationship to legitimate legislative ends, among them avoiding the necessity of trying stale claims. The court of appeals correctly concluded that the passenger did not adequately plead a continuing failure to warn.


OUTCOME: The order ruling that the statute of repose was constitutional and that the passenger did not allege a continuing failure to warn in his products liability action was affirmed.

Hunter v. Eugene

DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, teachers and a news reporter, filed a complaint in the United States District Court of Oregon against defendants, a city, officials, and police officers.


OVERVIEW: The teachers alleged that they were attacked by club-wielding city police officers acting within the scope of their employment and driven from their respective locations on or near a strike picket line at a high school. The teachers sought to impose liability for damages for the assaults on and arrests of the teachers, as well as to recover reasonable attorney fees. The court held that persons whose rights under Or. I, § 8, were violated by a municipality or its employees could not bring an action for damages against the municipality or its employees directly under the constitution, but would be limited to existing common-law, equitable, and statutory remedies. The court determined that if an implied private right of action for damages for governmental violations § 8, and other non-self-executing constitutional provisions were to exist, it was appropriate that it come from the legislature, not the court.


OUTCOME: The court held that the teachers were limited to existing common-law, equitable, and statutory remedies.

Multnomah County v. $5,650 in U.S. Currency


Nos. TC A8608-04859, A8512-07963, CA A48241 (Control), A48456 SC S36239, Cases Consolidated for Argument and Opinion Only


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 285; 786 P.2d 729; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 15


September 6, 1989, Argued and submitted  
January 31, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * No. A8512-07963; CA No. A48456; No. A8608-04859; CA No. A48241.


*  Appeal from judgments of Multnomah County Circuit Court, William Keys and Charles S. Crookham, Judges. 96 Or App 420, 774 P2d 489 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgments of the circuit court are reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Multnomah County Code § 7.85.005 et seq., petitioner Multnomah County brought in rem actions to enforce forfeitures of defendant assets, which were used in illegal activity involving the making or delivery of controlled substances within the County. Respondent property owners appeared as interested parties. Judgments of forfeiture were entered. The Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversed the judgments. The County sought review.


OVERVIEW: The County's forfeiture ordinance defined the terms "controlled substances," "delivery," "manufacture," "production," and "illegal activity" by reference to the state statutes imposing criminal penalties for producing and distributing specified drugs, Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 475. The property owners argued that the ordinance was unconstitutional and preempted by state law. On appeal, the court of appeals reversed the judgments of forfeiture. The County sought review, arguing that it had adopted a home rule charter under Or. Const. art. IX, § 10. Thus, the court of appeals erroneously held that it lacked authority to enact and enforce the forfeiture ordinances. The court granted review and affirmed the court of appeals' decision, reasoning that the county did not lack authority to enact the forfeiture ordinance nor did state law preempt the ordinance. But the remedies subject to adjudication in state court remained a matter of state law, not of home rule. Under former Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.315(3), the circuit court did not have authority to enforce the county's forfeiture ordinance to the extent that it was based on conduct that was defined and punishable as a crime under state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals. The judgments of the circuit court were reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss the County's forfeiture actions.

State v. Wagner


Nos. CC 85061212, SC S32635


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 5; 786 P.2d 93; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 3


August 14, 1989, Argued and submitted  
January 11, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On remand from the United States Supreme Court. * CC No. 85061212.


* Automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Circuit Court for Linn County. William O. Lewis, Judge. 305 Or 115, 752 P2d 1136 (1988), judgment vacated and remanded 492 U.S.   , 109 S Ct 3235, 106 L Ed 2d 583 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed as to the guilt phase and reversed as to the penalty phase. The case is remanded to the circuit court for resentencing for the reasons stated in this opinion and in accordance with the procedures outlined herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court vacated a judgment of the Oregon Supreme Court affirming defendant's death sentence for the crime of aggravated murder. The case was remanded to the state supreme court for further consideration in light of the United States Supreme Court's decision in Penry v. Lynaugh.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150 permitted the trial to submit to the sentencing jury a so-called "fourth question" of whether the death penalty was appropriate for defendant, considering all aspects of his life and crime. The court observed that § 163.150(1)(e), by its reference to issues considered under § 163.150, clearly included those issues submitted pursuant to § 163.150(1)(b), but did not preclude the submission and consideration of other issues. The court next concluded that § 163.150 permitted the introduction of all constitutionally relevant mitigation evidence beyond the scope of the statutory issues set forth in § 163.150(1)(b). In summation, the court found the statute was found facially constitutional as the trial court had authority under § 163.150(1) to submit a fourth question to the sentencing jury notwithstanding an affirmative finding on the issues listed in § 163.150(1)(b). Procedurally, defendant was entitled to a sentencing trial before a new sentencing jury. The court further directed that the new sentencing jury should be instructed to consider all aspects of defendant's character and background as independent mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court as to the guilt phase and reversed its judgment as to the penalty phase. The court remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Moen

SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


309 Ore. 45; 786 P.2d 111; 1990 Ore. LEXIS 6

Stat. § 163.150(1)(b)(B) and dangerousness to society. Transcripts of testimony from prior convictions were properly admitted because they met the criteria under Or. Evid. Code 804(3)(a) as former testimony. Defendant's Eighth Amendment challenges were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment to the guilt phase of defendant's conviction for aggravated murder. The court reversed and remanded the circuit court's order that imposed the death penalty on defendant.

No. SC S36443

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer petitioned for a writ of mandamus, seeking to have 1989 Or. The action was brought against defendants, governor, State Treasurer of the State of Oregon, Director of the Oregon Department of General Services, and Oregon Department of General Services.


OVERVIEW: 1989 Or. Laws 1032 authorized the Director of the Oregon Department of General Services, upon the approval of the State Treasurer of the State of Oregon and the Executive Department, to enter into certain financing agreements. Oregon State Police Officers Ass'n v. State


Nos. TC A8508-05041; CA A46148; SC S35924


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


308 Ore. 531; 783 P.2d 7; 1989 Ore. LEXIS 634


May 3, 1989, Argued and submitted  
November 30, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 11, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. A8508-05041; CA No. A46148.


*  Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Irving M. Steinbock, Judge. 94 Or App 478, 766 P2d 408 (1988).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The judgment of the circuit court holding that the political activity clause of ORS 181.400(2) violates Article I, section 8, of the Oregon Constitution, is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court awarding plaintiffs attorney fees is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, State of Oregon, Oregon Department of State Police, and Superintendent of State Police, disputed the affirmance by the Court of Appeals (Oregon) of a decision by a circuit court, which ruled that the political activity clause of Or. Rev. Stat. § 181.400(2) violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and awarded attorney fees to respondents, police employee organization and president, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that certain restrictions were already imposed on respondents by Or. Rev. Stat. § 260.432(2), to which they did not object. Petitioners, virtually conceding that § 181.400(2) was overbroad, argued that the Superintendent's guidelines brought the political activity clause within constitutional bounds. The court held that, in prohibiting any political activity or speech except voting, § 181.400(2) imposed restrictions that went far beyond any permissible limitation that the state could place on state police officers' art. I, § 8 rights. No limiting regulation could be both consistent with the express prohibition of § 181.400(2) against any political activity except voting and at the same time narrow the statute's scope within constitutional limits. Section 181.400(2) could not be saved by judicial or agency interpretation. The court held that the political activity clause of § 181.400(2) was overbroad in violation of art. I, § 8. But, because state remedies were adequate to protect respondents' rights, their invocation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was unnecessary, and attorney fees could not be awarded under § 1988. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals in part and reversed in part. The political activity clause was unconstitutional, but attorney fees should not have been awarded.

 

164 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Associated Oregon Veterans v. Department of Veterans' Affairs


Nos. CC 86C-12404; CA A46714/A47761; SC S35929/S35930 (cases consolidated for argument and opinion)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


308 Ore. 476; 782 P.2d 418; 1989 Ore. LEXIS 543


September 5, 1989, Argued and submitted  
November 16, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. 86C-12404; CA Nos. A46714, A47761.


*  Appeals from Circuit Court, Marion County Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. 94 Or App 510, 766 P2d 1040 (1988) (CA A46714). 94 Or App 526, 766 P2d 1043 (1988) (CA A47761).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals in case No. A46714 affirming the circuit court judgment is affirmed. In case No. A47761 the decision of the Court of Appeals affirming the circuit court judgment is modified and attorney fees are reduced to $ 27,318.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following remand, plaintiffs, veterans and association, challenged a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), affirming a summary judgment in favor of defendant Department of Veterans' Affairs (DVA), in an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, seeking a determination of rights under their farm and home loan agreements. Plaintiffs asserted that the DVA breached the loan agreements, and that an award of attorney fees was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought declaratory and injunctive relief in an action to determine their rights under farm and home loan agreements with the DVA. Following remand, the trial court granted summary judgment to the DVA, and the appellate court affirmed. Plaintiffs appealed, asserting that an increase in monthly payments constituted a breach of the loan agreements. In a separate appeal, they contested the award of attorney fees. The court affirmed the summary judgment, explaining that after the legislature had authorized DVA to increase its interest rates, DVA raised plaintiffs' rate and increased their monthly payments. In a prior appeal, the court agreed that the DVA could not increase monthly mortgage payments without the mortgagor's consent. In compliance with that holding, DVA gave plaintiffs the option of consenting to higher monthly payments or extending the amortization period. Plaintiffs opted to extend the amortization period. The loss of a pay-off date was due to this choice and not to a breach of the agreements. The court modified the award of attorney fees to reflect the amount of fees that were actually billed to the DVA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate decision affirming the summary judgment. It modified the award of attorney fees by reducing it to the amount for which the DVA was actually billed.

 

165 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Dennehy v. Department of Revenue


Nos. TC 2395, SC S35954


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


308 Ore. 423; 781 P.2d 346; 1989 Ore. LEXIS 540


September 7, 1989, Argued and submitted  
October 26, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Oregon Tax Court. Carl N. Byers, Judge. TC No. 2395.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Tax Court awarding attorney fees is reversed; the judgment of the Tax Court is otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Oregon Tax Court that failed to award refunds of taxes based upon improperly "rounded up" tax levy rates to members of the general public and failed to award the taxpayer an appropriate attorney fee. Respondent Department of Revenue, State of Oregon, appealed the award of any attorney fee.


OVERVIEW: On remand from a judgment that the Department's practice of "rounding up" property tax levy rates violated Or. Const. art. XI, § 11, the taxpayer sought refunds to the public at large and an award of attorney fees. The tax court refused to make any refund other than to the taxpayer but did award attorney fees. The taxpayer appealed, as did the Department. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court noted that the only statutory provision governing refunds to classes of taxpayers was Or. Rev. Stat. § 311.806(2) and found that, under the statute, the tax court had no authority to order the relief sought by the taxpayer. Such refund decisions were for the taxing authorities involved to make and the tax court's refusal to adjudicate refund claims for members of the general public in this proceeding was correct. As to the award of attorney fees, the court noted that an Oregon court could only award fees as provided for by contract or statute. The statute related to tax appeals, Or. Rev. Stat. § 305.490, did not apply to appeals concerning property tax assessments with the result that the tax court had no statutory authority to award attorney fees to the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: That portion of the tax court's judgment refusing to award refunds to the public at large was affirmed but its award of an attorney fee to the taxpayer was reversed.

 

166 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Samuel v. Frohnmayer


Nos. TC 137346, CA A47340, SC S36166


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


308 Ore. 362; 779 P.2d 1028; 1989 Ore. LEXIS 456


July 5, 1989, Argued and submitted  
September 19, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 11, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. * TC No. 137346; CA No. A47340.


*  Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Duane R. Ertsgaard, Judge. 95 Or App 561, 770 P2d 914 (1989).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractor appealed an order of the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which reversed the trial court's award of attorney fees to the chiropractor as expenses incurred in his successfully pursuing a declaratory judgment against defendant state attorney general under Or. Rev. Stat. § 28.080.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor chaired a peer review committee established upon the request of a state agency. Another chiropractor reviewed by the committee brought suit for damages. The chiropractor successfully obtained a declaration that the attorney general was obliged to take defense of the earlier case. The chiropractor then sought his attorney fees as "further relief." The court reversed, finding that state law did not permit a trial court to award attorney fees unless there was authority to do so in a statute or contract and that the only statute authorizing attorney fee awards against the attorney general, Or. Rev. Stat. § 182.090, did not apply here. The court held that where a particular statute, here Or. Rev. Stat. § 182.090, provided for a remedy such as the award of attorney fees by a court to a successful litigant and where that statute established particular conditions for its application, it was inappropriate for a court to import into another, more general statute, here Or. Rev. Stat. § 28.080, the same or even broader authority to award attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court and affirmed the judgment of the trial court that the chiropractor was not entitled to attorney fees for successfully obtaining a declaratory judgment against the state attorney general.

 

167 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Glerum v. Roberts


No. SC S36147


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


308 Ore. 22; 774 P.2d 1093; 1989 Ore. LEXIS 134


May 18, 1989, Argued and submitted  
May 26, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petition to review ballot title.



DISPOSITION: Ballot title certified as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed an action against respondent secretary of state challenging a ballot title for a proposed constitutional amendment on the grounds that the legislature's ballot title was insufficient and misleading and failed to substantially comply with Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.035.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners challenged the ballot title to a proposed constitutional amendment relating to a prohibition on the sale or export of timber from certain lands unless such timber would be processed in the state. Petitioners alleged that the ballot title, which consisted of a caption, question, and explanation, failed to substantially comply with § 250.035. The court modified the title and certified it. The court found that the caption erroneously substituted the word "logs" for the word "timber," as "timber" was the word actually used in the measure and "timber" had a much broader meaning than "logs." The court found that the question portion of the title had to phrase the measure's chief purpose, and that the question failed because it substituted the words "sale for export" for "sale or export," which was the language used in the measure. The court held that the explanation section of the title was required to mention the exemption on the sale or export prohibition for particular species, grades, or quantities of timber in certain circumstances, as such exemption softened the otherwise total prohibition and aided in summarizing the measure properly.


OUTCOME: The court modified the ballot title and certified it as modified.

 

168 of 1650 DOCUMENTS


Lloyd Corp. v. Whiffen


SC No. S35170


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


307 Ore. 674; 773 P.2d 1294; 1989 Ore. LEXIS 129


September 7, 1988, Argued and submitted  
May 9, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review from the Court of Appeals. * CC No. A8512-08127; CA No. A38839.


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Kristena A. LaMar, Judge. 89 Or App 629, 750 P2d 1157 (1988).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed, but on different grounds. The decision of the trial court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Oregon) reversed the decision of the trial court, which enjoined defendant solicitors from entering upon plaintiff shopping center owner's private property to exercise their expressions of opinion or to gather signatures in the initiative and referendum process without the shopping center's permission or consent. The shopping center owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: In reversing, the court of appeals held that the order violated the solicitors' rights of expression under Or. Const. art. I, § 8 and that the solicitors could have exercised their free expression rights in the shopping center subject to reasonable regulations. The record supported the shopping center owner's (owner) contention that it had attempted to limit access of persons whose purpose was not to shop or do business with the tenants. The court noted that Or. Rev. Stat. § 250 recognized a right to seek signatures of others and a strong public interest in facilitating that process. The court held that if the solicitors were denied access to the owner's private property, the public interest served by the solicitors' activity would have sustained serious injury. Equity simply could not have spread a complete blanket over all political activity. The solicitation of signatures of patrons did not in and of itself constitute substantial interference. The public policy behind the signature-gathering process limited equitable enforcement of plaintiff's preferred total exclusion of signature solicitors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, but on different grounds.
